`README.md`:

```md
# ephemera

Multiplatform windows kernel crash dump analysis tool with a WinDbg flavor.

### Motivation

This is another episode from the series "there doesn't seem to exist such
thing".

I often find myself needing to analyze Windows kernel crash dumps on non-Windows
platforms. Surprisingly, WinDbg/cdb <abbr title="doesn't run at all">runs rather
poorly under Wine</abbr>. Also, even on Windows, WinDbg is notoriously slow.

I also thought this would be a fun showcase for the [vmi-rs] framework.

Initially, I planned to make `ephemera` a general-purpose memory forensics
framework - similar to Volatility or Rekall - but I quickly realized that the
scope of such a project is incompatible with the amount of time I can
realistically dedicate to this.

Maybe, some day. Who knows.

### Features

- Supports symbol caching and PDB downloading/parsing via the [`isr`].
- Supports only Windows kernel crash dumps (i.e. `MEMORY.DMP` files).
- Supports only AMD64 architecture.
- Supports only a small subset of WinDbg commands (see below).
- It's fast. Really fast. `!process 0 7` takes _minutes_ in WinDbg.
  In `ephemera`, it takes about 1 second on a 4GB dump (if all symbols are
  already cached).

### Demo

<video src="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/13cd6e4e-cfef-44c5-83a5-c984e2cd7c97" controls autoplay loop></video>

### Usage

Here's a short list of currently supported commands:

```
Commands:
  !analyze                             Analyze the crash.
  !process [Proc [Flags [Image]]]      Information about a process or all processes.
                                       Proc: PID, EPROCESS addr, 0 (all), -1 (current).
  !thread  [Thread [Flags]]            Information about a thread or all threads.
                                       Thread: TID, ETHREAD addr, 0 (all), -1 (current).
  dt <type> [address]                  Display type layout, optionally at an address.
  db  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]  Display memory as bytes and ASCII.
                                       Address: hex, 0n<decimal>, register, or module!symbol.
                                                Arithmetic: a+b, a-b. Empty module means nt.
  dd  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]  Display memory as DWORDs.
  dq  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]  Display memory as QWORDs.
  dp  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]  Alias for dq on 64-bit.
  dps [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]  Display memory as QWORDs with symbols.
  k  [FrameCount]                      Display stack backtrace: Child-SP, RetAddr, Call Site.
  kb [FrameCount]                      As k, plus the first four home-space args per frame.
  kc [FrameCount]                      As k, Call Site only.
  kv [FrameCount]                      As kb, plus TrapFrame @ addr for trap-handler frames.
  r [Reg]                              Display registers.
                                       Reg: rax..r15, rip, rsp, rbp, cs/ds/es/fs/gs/ss, efl.
  .process [/r] [/p] <address>         Set the process context.
  .thread  [/r] [/p] <address>         Set the register context to a thread.
  ~<n>                                 Change the current processor.
  .help, help, ?                       Show this list.
  q, quit, .quit                       Exit the REPL.
```

### FAQ

- Could it be made into a full-fledged debugger, with support for live
 debugging, breakpoints, ...?

  > Yes! Quite easily, actually. `vmi-rs` supports multiple backend drivers,
  > so it's just a matter of replacing [`VmiKdmpDriver`] with [something else].
  > Implementing a new driver is also pretty straightforward - for read-only
  > operations you only need to implement [`VmiRead`] trait.

# License

This project is licensed under the MIT license.

[vmi-rs]: https://github.com/vmi-rs/vmi
[isr]: https://github.com/vmi-rs/isr
[Volatility]: https://github.com/volatilityfoundation/volatility3
[Rekall]: https://github.com/google/rekall
[`VmiRead`]: https://docs.rs/vmi/latest/vmi/trait.VmiRead.html
[`VmiKdmpDriver`]: https://docs.rs/vmi/0.6.0/vmi/driver/kdmp/struct.VmiKdmpDriver.html
[something else]: https://docs.rs/vmi/0.6.0/vmi/driver/index.html

```

`assets/bugcheck.yaml`:

```yaml
# Windows Bugcheck Database
# Extracted from ext.dll (WinDbg extension)
# Format matches WinDbg !analyze -show output
#
# For bugchecks with context-dependent arg descriptions,
# the "variants" list provides per-subcode descriptions.
# The "when" field specifies which parameter value triggers that variant.

bugchecks:

  - code: 0x00000001
    name: APC_INDEX_MISMATCH
    description: |
      This is a kernel internal error. The most common reason to see this
      BugCheck is when a filesystem or a driver has a mismatched number of
      calls to disable and re-enable APCs. The key data item is the
      Thread->CombinedApcDisable field. This consists of two separate 16-bit
      fields, the SpecialApcDisable and the KernelApcDisable. A negative value
      of either indicates that a driver has disabled special or normal APCs
      (respectively) without re-enabling them; a positive value indicates that
      a driver has enabled special or normal APCs (respectively) too many times.
    args:
      arg1: Address of system call function or worker routine
      arg2: "Thread->ApcStateIndex"
      arg3: "(Thread->SpecialApcDisable << 16) | Thread->KernelApcDisable"
      arg4: "Call type (0 - system call, 1 - worker routine)"

  - code: 0x00000002
    name: DEVICE_QUEUE_NOT_BUSY
    description: ""
    args:
      arg1: ~
      arg2: ~
      arg3: ~
      arg4: ~

    name: INVALID_AFFINITY_SET
    description: ""
    args:
      arg1: ~
      arg2: ~
      arg3: ~
      arg4: ~

      interrupt request level (IRQL) that is too high.  This is usually
      caused by drivers using improper addresses.
      If a kernel debugger is available get the stack backtrace.
    args:
      arg1: memory referenced
      arg2: IRQL
      arg3: |
        bitfield :
        	bit 0 : value 0 = read operation, 1 = write operation
        	bit 3 : value 0 = not an execute operation, 1 = execute operation (only on chips which support this level of status)
      arg4: address which referenced memory

  - code: 0x0000000B
    name: NO_EXCEPTION_HANDLING_SUPPORT

    variants:
      - when: {arg1: 0x01}
        args:

          arg4: ~

      - when: {arg1: 0x05}

  - code: 0x00000018
    name: REFERENCE_BY_POINTER
    description: ""
    args:
      arg1: Object type of the object whose reference count is being lowered
      arg2: Object whose reference count is being lowered
      arg3: Reserved
      arg4: |
        Reserved
        	The reference count of an object is illegal for the current state of the object.
        	Each time a driver uses a pointer to an object the driver calls a kernel routine
        	to increment the reference count of the object. When the driver is done with the
        	pointer the driver calls another kernel routine to decrement the reference count.
        	Drivers must match calls to the increment and decrement routines. This BugCheck
        	can occur because an object's reference count goes to zero while there are still
        	open handles to the object, in which case the fourth parameter indicates the number
        	of opened handles. It may also occur when the object's reference count drops below zero
        	whether or not there are open handles to the object, and in that case the fourth parameter
        	contains the actual value of the pointer references count.

  - code: 0x00000020
    name: KERNEL_APC_PENDING_DURING_EXIT
    description: |
      The key data item is the thread's APC disable count.
      If this is non-zero, then this is the source of the problem.
      The APC disable count is decremented each time a driver calls
      KeEnterCriticalRegion, FsRtlEnterFileSystem, or acquires a mutex.  The APC
      disable count is incremented each time a driver calls KeLeaveCriticalRegion,
      FsRtlExitFileSystem, or KeReleaseMutex.  Since these calls should always be in
      pairs, this value should be zero when a thread exits.  A negative value
      indicates that a driver has disabled APC calls without re-enabling them.  A
      positive value indicates that the reverse is true.
      If you ever see this error, be very suspicious of all drivers installed on the
      machine -- especially unusual or non-standard drivers.  Third party file
      system redirectors are especially suspicious since they do not generally
      receive the heavy duty testing that NTFS, FAT, RDR, etc receive.
      This current IRQL should also be 0.  If it is not, that a driver's
      cancellation routine can cause this BugCheck by returning at an elevated
      IRQL.  Always attempt to note what you were doing/closing at the
      time of the crash, and note all of the installed drivers at the time of
      the crash.  This symptom is usually a severe bug in a third party
      driver.
    args:
      arg1: The address of the APC found pending during exit.
      arg2: "The thread's APC disable count"
      arg3: ~
      arg4: ~

      stack for the current request can be found by examining the DeviceObject

  - code: 0x0000004C
    name: FATAL_UNHANDLED_HARD_ERROR
    description: |
      If a hard error occurs during system booting before windows is up, and
      the hard error is a real error, the system will blue screen crash.
      Some common cases are:
          x218 - This means a necessary registry hive file could not be
                 loaded.  The obvious reason is if it is corrupt or missing.
                 In this case, either the Emergency Repair Disk or a
                 reinstall is required.
                 Some less obvious reasons are that the driver has corrupted
                 the registry data while loading into memory, or the memory
                 where the registry file was loaded is not actually memory.
          x21a - This means that either winlogon, or csrss (windows) died
                 unexpectedly.  The exit code tells more information.  Usually
                 it is c0000005 meaning that an unhandled exception crashed
                 either of these processes.
          x221 - This means that a driver is corrupt, or a system DLL was
                 detected to be corrupt.
                 Safeboot or boot an alternate OS (or reinstall)
                 and then make sure the on disk file that is listed as bad
                 matches the version on CD and replace if necessary.  In some
                 cases, random corruption can mean that there is a hardware
                 problem in the I/O path to the file.
    args:
      arg1: ~
      arg2: ~
      arg3: ~
      arg4: ~

  - code: 0x0000004D
    name: NO_PAGES_AVAILABLE
    description: |
      No free pages available to continue operations.
      If kernel debugger available \"!vm 3\".
              This BugCheck can occur for the following reasons:
              1.  A driver has blocked, deadlocking the modified or mapped
                  page writers.  Examples of this include mutex deadlocks or
                  accesses to paged out memory in filesystem drivers, filter
                  drivers, etc.  This indicates a driver bug.
                  If parameter 1 or 2 is large, then this is a possibility.  Type
                  \"!vm 3\" in the kernel debugger.
              2.  The storage driver(s) are not processing requests.  Examples
                  of this are stranded queues, non-responding drives, etc.  This
                  indicates a driver bug.
                  If parameter 1 or 2 is large, then this is a possibility.  Type
                  \"!process 0 7\" in the kernel debugger.
              3.  Not enough pool is available for the storage stack to write out
                  modified pages.  This indicates a driver bug.
                  If parameter 3 is small, then this is a possibility.  Type
                  \"!vm\" and \"!poolused 2\" in the kernel debugger.
              4.  A high priority realtime thread has starved the balance set
                  manager from trimming pages and/or starved the modified writer
                  from writing them out.  This indicates a bug in the component
                  that created this thread.
                  This one is hard to determine, try \"!ready\"
              5.  All the processes have been trimmed to their minimums and all
                  modified pages written, but still no memory is available.  The
                  freed memory must be stuck in transition pages with non-zero
                  reference counts - thus they cannot be put on the freelist.
                  A driver is neglecting to unlock the pages preventing the
                  reference counts from going to zero which would free the pages.
                  This may be due to transfers that never finish and the driver
                  never aborts or other driver bugs.
                  If parameter 4 is large, then this is a possibility.  But it
                  is very hard to find the driver.  Try \"!process 0 1\" and look
                  for any that have a lot of locked pages.
      If the problem cannot be found, then try booting with /DEBUG and a kernel
      debugger attached, so if it reproduces, a debug session can be initiated
      to identify the cause.
    args:
      arg1: Total number of dirty pages
      arg2: Number of dirty pages destined for the pagefile(s).
      arg3: Internal flags.
      arg4: Most recent modified write error status.

  - code: 0x0000007B
    name: INACCESSIBLE_BOOT_DEVICE
    description: |
      During the initialization of the I/O system, it is possible that the driver
      for the boot device failed to initialize the device that the system is
      attempting to boot from, or it is possible for the file system that is
      supposed to read that device to either fail its initialization or to simply
      not recognize the data on the boot device as a file system structure that
      it recognizes.  In the former case, the argument (#1) is the address of a
      Unicode string data structure that is the ARC name of the device from which
      the boot was being attempted.  In the latter case, the argument (#1) is the
      address of the device object that could not be mounted.
      If this is the initial setup of the system, then this error can occur if
      the system was installed on an unsupported disk or SCSI controller.  Note
      that some controllers are supported only by drivers which are in the Windows
      Driver Library (WDL) which requires the user to do a custom install.  See
      the Windows Driver Library for more information.
      This error can also be caused by the installation of a new SCSI adapter or
      disk controller or repartitioning the disk with the system partition.  If
      this is the case, on x86 systems the boot.ini file must be edited or on ARC
      systems setup must be run.  See the \"Advanced Server System Administrator's
      User Guide\" for information on changing boot.ini.
      If the argument is a pointer to an ARC name string, then the format of the
      first two (and in this case only) longwords will be:
          USHORT Length;
          USHORT MaximumLength;
          PWSTR Buffer;
      That is, the first longword will contain something like 00800020 where 20
      is the actual length of the Unicode string, and the next longword will
      contain the address of buffer.  This address will be in system space, so
      the high order bit will be set.
      If the argument is a pointer to a device object, then the format of the first
      word will be:
          USHORT Type;
      That is, the first word will contain a 0003, where the Type code will ALWAYS
      be 0003.
      Note that this makes it immediately obvious whether the argument is a pointer
      to an ARC name string or a device object, since a Unicode string can never
      have an odd number of bytes, and a device object will always have a Type
      code of 3.
    args:
      arg1: Pointer to the device object or Unicode string of ARC name
      arg2: (reserved)
      arg3: (reserved)
      arg4: (reserved)

  - code: 0x00000096
    name: INVALID_WORK_QUEUE_ITEM
    description: |
      This message occurs when KeRemoveQueue removes a queue entry whose flink
      or blink field is null.  This is almost always called by code misusing
      worker thread work items, but any queue misuse can cause this.  The rule
      is that an entry on a queue may only be inserted on the list once. When an
      item is removed from a queue, it's flink field is set to NULL. This BugCheck
      occurs when remove queue attempts to remove an entry, but the flink or blink
      field is NULL. In order to debug this problem, you need to know the queue being
      referenced.
      In an attempt to help identify the guilty driver, this BugCheck assumes the
      queue is a worker queue (ExWorkerQueue) and prints the worker routine as
      parameter 4 below.
    args:
      arg1: The address of the queue entry whose flink/blink field is NULL
      arg2: |
        The address of the queue being references. Usually this is one
        	of the ExWorkerQueues.
      arg3: |
        The base address of the ExWorkerQueue array. This will help determine
        	if the queue in question is an ExWorkerQueue and if so, the offset from
        	this parameter will isolate the queue.
      arg4: |
        If this is an ExWorkerQueue (which it usually is), this is the address
        	of the worker routine that would have been called if the work item was
        	valid. This can be used to isolate the driver that is misusing the work
        	queue.

    name: MACHINE_CHECK_EXCEPTION
    description: |
      A fatal Machine Check Exception has occurred.
      KeBugCheckEx parameters;
          x86 Processors
              If the processor has ONLY MCE feature available (For example Intel
              Pentium), the parameters are:
              1 - Low  32 bits of P5_MC_TYPE MSR
              2 - Address of MCA_EXCEPTION structure
              3 - High 32 bits of P5_MC_ADDR MSR
              4 - Low  32 bits of P5_MC_ADDR MSR
              If the processor also has MCA feature available (For example Intel
              Pentium Pro), the parameters are:
              1 - Bank number
              2 - Address of MCA_EXCEPTION structure
              3 - High 32 bits of MCi_STATUS MSR for the MCA bank that had the error
              4 - Low  32 bits of MCi_STATUS MSR for the MCA bank that had the error
          IA64 Processors
              1 - BugCheck Type
                  1 - MCA_ASSERT
                  2 - MCA_GET_STATEINFO
                      SAL returned an error for SAL_GET_STATEINFO while processing MCA.
                  3 - MCA_CLEAR_STATEINFO
                      SAL returned an error for SAL_CLEAR_STATEINFO while processing MCA.
                  4 - MCA_FATAL
                      FW reported a fatal MCA.
                  5 - MCA_NONFATAL
                      SAL reported a recoverable MCA and we don't support currently
                      support recovery or SAL generated an MCA and then couldn't
                      produce an error record.
                  0xB - INIT_ASSERT
                  0xC - INIT_GET_STATEINFO
                        SAL returned an error for SAL_GET_STATEINFO while processing INIT event.
                  0xD - INIT_CLEAR_STATEINFO
                        SAL returned an error for SAL_CLEAR_STATEINFO while processing INIT event.
                  0xE - INIT_FATAL
                        Not used.
              2 - Address of log
              3 - Size of log
              4 - Error code in the case of x_GET_STATEINFO or x_CLEAR_STATEINFO
          AMD64 Processors (If Param 1 is < 0x80000000)
              1 - Bank number
              2 - Address of MCA_EXCEPTION structure
              3 - High 32 bits of MCi_STATUS MSR for the MCA bank that had the error
              4 - Low  32 bits of MCi_STATUS MSR for the MCA bank that had the error

              1 - Failure Type

                      0x80000001: Spurious MCE

                      0x80000002: Rendezvous failure

  - code: 0x000000EA
    name: THREAD_STUCK_IN_DEVICE_DRIVER
    description: |
      The device driver is spinning in an infinite loop, most likely waiting for
      hardware to become idle. This usually indicates problem with the hardware
      itself or with the device driver programming the hardware incorrectly.
      If the kernel debugger is connected and running when watchdog detects a
      timeout condition then DbgBreakPoint() will be called instead of KeBugCheckEx()
      and detailed message including BugCheck arguments will be printed to the
      debugger. This way we can identify an offending thread, set breakpoints in it,
      and hit go to return to the spinning code to debug it further. Because
      KeBugCheckEx() is not called the .BugCheck directive will not return BugCheck
      information in this case. The arguments are already printed out to the kernel
      debugger. You can also retrieve them from a global variable via
      \"dd watchdog!g_WdBugCheckData l5\" (use dq on NT64).
      On MP machines (OS builds <= 3790) it is possible to hit a timeout when the spinning thread is
      interrupted by hardware interrupt and ISR or DPC routine is running at the time
      of the BugCheck (this is because the timeout's work item can be delivered and
      handled on the second CPU and the same time). If this is the case you will have
      to look deeper at the offending thread's stack (e.g. using dds) to determine
      spinning code which caused the timeout to occur.
    args:
      arg1: |
        Pointer to a stuck thread object.  Do .thread then kb on it to find
        	the hung location.
      arg2: Pointer to a DEFERRED_WATCHDOG object.
      arg3: Pointer to offending driver name.
      arg4: |
        Number of times this error occurred.  If a debugger is attached,
        	this error is not always fatal -- see DESCRIPTION below.  On the
        	blue screen, this will always equal 1.

  - code: 0x000000F2
    name: HARDWARE_INTERRUPT_STORM
    description: |
      Note:  This BugCheck no longer exists in any version of Windows.
      This BugCheck will show up on the screen when the kernel
      detects an interrupt \"storm\".  An interrupt storm is defined as a level
      triggered interrupt signal staying in the asserted state.  This is fatal
      to the system in the manner that the system will hard hang, or \"bus lock\".
      This can happen because of the following:
       -  A piece of hardware does not release its interrupt signal after being told
          to do so by the device driver
       -  A device driver does not instruct its hardware to release the interrupt
          signal because it does not believe the interrupt was initiated from its
          hardware
       -  A device driver claims the interrupt even though the interrupt was not
          initiated from its hardware.  Note that this can only occur when multiple
          devices are sharing the same IRQ.
       -  The ELCR (edge level control register) is set incorrectly.
       -  Edge and Level interrupt triggered devices share an IRQ (e.g. COM port and
          PCI SCSI controller).
      All of these cases will instantly hard hang your system.  Instead of hard
      hanging the system, this BugCheck is initiated since in many cases it can
      identify the culprit.
      When the BugCheck occurs, the module containing the ISR (interrupt service
      routine) of the storming IRQ is displayed on the screen.  This is an
      example of what you would see:
      *** STOP: 0x000000F2 (0xFCA7C55C, 0x817B9B28, 0x817D2AA0, 0x00000002)
      An interrupt storm has caused the system to hang.
      *** Address FCA7C55C base at FCA72000, Datestamp 3A72BDEF - ACPI.sys
      In the event the fourth parameter is a 0x00000001, the module pointed to
      is very likely the culprit.  Either the driver is broken, or the hardware
      is malfunctioning.
      In the event the fourth parameter is a 0x00000002, the module pointed to
      is the first ISR in the chain, and is never guaranteed to be the culprit.
      A user experiencing this BugCheck repeatedly should try to isolate the
      problem by looking for devices that are on the same IRQ as the one for
      which the module is a driver for (in this case, the same IRQ that ACPI
      is using).  In the future, we may be able to list all devices on a
      chained ISR.
    args:
      arg1: address of the ISR (or first ISR in the chain) connected to the storming interrupt vector
      arg2: ISR context value
      arg3: address of the interrupt object for the storming interrupt vector
      arg4: "0x1 if the ISR is not chained, 0x2 if the ISR is chained"

      may block critical user mode components without blocking DPCs or
      draining the nonpaged pool.

      to terminate this application and will keep monitoring if termination completes
      in time. If termination does not complete in time then machine will be BugChecked

      The device driver is spinning in an infinite loop, most likely waiting for
      hardware to become idle. This usually indicates problem with the hardware
      itself or with the device driver programming the hardware incorrectly.
      If the kernel debugger is connected and running when watchdog detects a
      timeout condition then DbgBreakPoint() will be called instead of KeBugCheckEx()
      and detailed message including BugCheck arguments will be printed to the
      debugger. This way we can identify an offending thread, set breakpoints in it,
      and hit go to return to the spinning code to debug it further. Because
      KeBugCheckEx() is not called the .BugCheck directive will not return BugCheck
      information in this case. The arguments are already printed out to the kernel
      debugger. You can also retrieve them from a global variable via
      \"dd watchdog!g_WdBugCheckData l5\" (use dq on NT64).
      On MP machines it is possible to hit a timeout when the spinning thread is
      interrupted by hardware interrupt and ISR or DPC routine is running at the time
      of the BugCheck (this is because the timeout's work item can be delivered and
      handled on the second CPU and the same time). If this is the case you will have
      to look deeper at the offending thread's stack (e.g. using dds) to determine
      spinning code which caused the timeout to occur.

      is running on being terminated. Look at the callstack. If there is
      a driver on the stack that is directly followed by system exception
      handling routines and then thread termination routines, this driver
      is at fault and needs to be fixed so that it does not cause an
      unhandled exception while holding a kernel mutex. If the stack just
      shows normal thread termination code and no driver is implicated, run
      !pool or 'ln' on the address of the mutex (parameter 2) and see if you
```

`src/cli/bugcheck.rs`:

```rs
//! Bugcheck database loaded from `assets/bugcheck.yaml`.
//!
//! Provides lookup by bugcheck code, with variant matching based on
//! the bugcheck parameters (the `when` field in the YAML).

use std::collections::HashMap;

use serde::Deserialize;

static BUGCHECK_YAML: &str = include_str!("../../assets/bugcheck.yaml");

pub struct BugcheckDb {
    entries: HashMap<u32, BugcheckEntry>,
}

impl BugcheckDb {
    /// Looks up a bugcheck by code. Returns the entry and, if one matches,
    /// the matching variant for the given parameters.
    pub fn lookup(
        &self,
        code: u32,
        params: [u64; 4],
    ) -> Option<(&BugcheckEntry, Option<&Variant>)> {
        let entry = self.entries.get(&code)?;
        let variant = entry
            .variants
            .iter()
            .flatten()
            .find(|variant| variant.matches(params));
        Some((entry, variant))
    }
}

pub fn load() -> BugcheckDb {
    let raw =
        serde_yaml::from_str::<BugcheckFile>(BUGCHECK_YAML).expect("failed to parse bugcheck.yaml");

    BugcheckDb {
        entries: raw
            .bugchecks
            .into_iter()
            .map(|entry| (entry.code, entry))
            .collect(),
    }
}

#[derive(Deserialize)]
struct BugcheckFile {
    bugchecks: Vec<BugcheckEntry>,
}

#[derive(Deserialize)]
pub struct BugcheckEntry {
    pub code: u32,
    pub name: String,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub description: String,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub args: ArgDescriptions,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub variants: Option<Vec<Variant>>,
}

#[derive(Deserialize, Default)]
pub struct ArgDescriptions {
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg1: Option<String>,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg2: Option<String>,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg3: Option<String>,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg4: Option<String>,
}

#[derive(Deserialize)]
pub struct Variant {
    pub when: WhenClause,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub args: ArgDescriptions,
}

/// A condition that matches on one of the bugcheck parameters.
#[derive(Deserialize)]
pub struct WhenClause {
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg1: Option<u64>,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg2: Option<u64>,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg3: Option<u64>,
    #[serde(default)]
    pub arg4: Option<u64>,
}

impl Variant {
    fn matches(&self, params: [u64; 4]) -> bool {
        self.when.arg1.is_none_or(|v| v == params[0])
            && self.when.arg2.is_none_or(|v| v == params[1])
            && self.when.arg3.is_none_or(|v| v == params[2])
            && self.when.arg4.is_none_or(|v| v == params[3])
    }
}

```

`src/cli/commands/analyze.rs`:

```rs
//! Analyze command (`!analyze -v`).
//!
//! Produces WinDbg-compatible output summarizing a crash dump:
//! bugcheck code and parameters, faulting process/thread, stack trace,
//! symbol name, and OS version information.

use std::io::Write;

use ephemera::{ResolvedSymbol, UnwindTarget, WalkFrame};
use vmi::{
    Va, VmiRead,
    arch::amd64::Amd64,
    driver::kdmp::Header64,
    os::{ProcessObject, ThreadObject, VmiOsProcess as _},
};

use crate::cli::{
    bugcheck::{self, ArgDescriptions, BugcheckDb},
    commands::HelpEntry,
    engine::Engine,
    format::{FormatModuleName, FormatSymbol, FormatVa},
    repl::ReplError,
};

/// Help text for `!analyze`.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[HelpEntry {
    syntax: "!analyze",
    summary: "Analyze the crash.",
    extra: &[],
}];

/// Runs the `!analyze -v` command.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    target: &UnwindTarget,
    header: &Header64,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let session = engine.ephemera();
    let process_object = target.process_object;

    // Print bugcheck code and parameters.
    let bugcheck = bugcheck::load();
    print_bugcheck(w, &bugcheck, header)?;
    writeln!(w)?;

    // Print faulting process name.
    let process = vmi.os().process(process_object)?;
    let process_name = process.name().unwrap_or_else(|_| "<unknown>".to_string());
    writeln!(w, "PROCESS_NAME:  {process_name}")?;
    writeln!(w)?;

    let thread_object = engine.current_thread();
    writeln!(w, "FAULTING_THREAD:  {thread_object:016x}")?;
    writeln!(w)?;

    // Walk the stack and collect frames for analysis.
    let mut frames = Vec::new();
    for frame_result in ephemera::walk_stack(vmi, session, target.clone()) {
        let frame = match frame_result {
            Ok(frame) => frame,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "unwind failed");
                break;
            }
        };

        let call_site = match session.lookup_module(vmi, process_object, frame.call_site)? {
            Some(module) => session.resolve_symbol(vmi, &module, frame.call_site),
            None => ResolvedSymbol {
                module_name: String::new(),
                function_name: String::new(),
                offset: frame.call_site.0,
            },
        };

        frames.push((frame, call_site));
    }

    // Print the stack.
    print_stack(w, &frames)?;
    writeln!(w)?;

    // Find the symbol name: the first frame after KeBugCheckEx
    // (the frame that called into the bugcheck path).
    let symbol_info = find_faulting_symbol(&frames);
    if let Some(symbol) = &symbol_info {
        writeln!(w, "SYMBOL_NAME:  {}", FormatSymbol(symbol))?;
        writeln!(w, "MODULE_NAME: {}", FormatModuleName(&symbol.module_name))?;
        // IMAGE_NAME is the raw DLL/EXE name (before FormatModuleName normalization).
        writeln!(w, "IMAGE_NAME:  {}", symbol.module_name)?;
    }
    writeln!(w)?;

    // Print the stack command.
    print_stack_command(w, process_object, thread_object)?;
    writeln!(w)?;

    // Print OS information.
    print_os_info(w, header)?;

    Ok(())
}

/// Prints bugcheck code, name, description, and parameter descriptions.
///
/// Uses the bugcheck database from `assets/bugchecks.yaml` to resolve
/// the bugcheck name and per-argument descriptions. When the bugcheck
/// has variants (keyed by `when`), the matching variant's argument
/// descriptions override the defaults.
fn print_bugcheck(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    bugcheck: &BugcheckDb,
    header: &Header64,
) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let code = header.bug_check_code();
    let params = [
        header.bug_check_parameter1(),
        header.bug_check_parameter2(),
        header.bug_check_parameter3(),
        header.bug_check_parameter4(),
    ];

    let entry = bugcheck.lookup(code, params);

    // Header line: NAME (code)
    match &entry {
        Some((entry, _)) => writeln!(w, "{} ({:x})", entry.name, code)?,
        None => writeln!(w, "UNKNOWN_BUGCHECK ({code:x})")?,
    }

    // Description.
    if let Some((entry, _)) = &entry {
        let desc = entry.description.trim();
        if !desc.is_empty() {
            writeln!(w, "{desc}")?;
        }
    }

    writeln!(w)?;
    writeln!(w, "BUGCHECK_CODE:  {code:x}")?;
    writeln!(w)?;

    // Pick argument descriptions: variant overrides base if present.
    let (base_args, variant_args) = match &entry {
        Some((entry, Some(variant))) => (Some(&entry.args), Some(&variant.args)),
        Some((entry, None)) => (Some(&entry.args), None),
        None => (None, None),
    };

    for (i, &param) in params.iter().enumerate() {
        let desc = pick_arg_desc(variant_args, i).or_else(|| pick_arg_desc(base_args, i));

        write!(w, "BUGCHECK_P{}: {}", i + 1, Va(param))?;
        if let Some(desc) = desc {
            write!(w, "  ({desc})")?;
        }
        writeln!(w)?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Returns the argument description for the given index from an
/// [`ArgDescriptions`], if present.
fn pick_arg_desc(args: Option<&ArgDescriptions>, index: usize) -> Option<&str> {
    let args = args?;

    match index {
        0 => args.arg1.as_deref(),
        1 => args.arg2.as_deref(),
        2 => args.arg3.as_deref(),
        3 => args.arg4.as_deref(),
        _ => None,
    }
}

/// Prints the stack trace in WinDbg format.
fn print_stack(w: &mut dyn Write, frames: &[(WalkFrame, ResolvedSymbol)]) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    writeln!(w, "STACK_TEXT:")?;
    for (frame, symbol) in frames {
        writeln!(
            w,
            "{} {} : {}",
            FormatVa(Va(frame.frame.stack_pointer.0)),
            FormatVa(frame.frame.instruction_pointer),
            FormatSymbol(symbol),
        )?;
    }
    Ok(())
}

/// Finds the "faulting symbol" - the first frame after KeBugCheckEx.
///
/// This is the frame that called into the bugcheck path, which WinDbg
/// reports as SYMBOL_NAME.
fn find_faulting_symbol(frames: &[(WalkFrame, ResolvedSymbol)]) -> Option<&ResolvedSymbol> {
    let mut found_bugcheck = false;
    for (_frame, symbol) in frames {
        if found_bugcheck {
            return Some(symbol);
        }
        if symbol.function_name.contains("KeBugCheck") {
            found_bugcheck = true;
        }
    }

    // If we did not find KeBugCheckEx, return the first frame.
    frames.first().map(|(_, symbol)| symbol)
}

/// Prints the stack command for reproducing the context in WinDbg.
fn print_stack_command(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    process: ProcessObject,
    thread: ThreadObject,
) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    writeln!(
        w,
        "STACK_COMMAND:  .process /r /p 0x{process:016x}; .thread /r /p 0x{thread:016x} ; kb"
    )
}

/// Prints OS version information derived from the dump header.
fn print_os_info(w: &mut dyn Write, header: &Header64) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let build = header.minor_version();
    let (os_name, os_major, os_minor) = os_version_from_build(build);

    writeln!(w, "OS_VERSION:  {os_major}.{os_minor}.{build}")?;
    writeln!(w, "OSNAME:  {os_name}")?;

    let platform = match header.machine_image_type() {
        0x014c => "x86",
        0x8664 => "x64",
        0xAA64 => "ARM64",
        _ => "unknown",
    };
    writeln!(w, "OSPLATFORM_TYPE:  {platform}")?;

    Ok(())
}

/// Maps an NT build number to (OS name, major version, minor version).
fn os_version_from_build(build: u32) -> (&'static str, u32, u32) {
    match build {
        build if build >= 22000 => ("Windows 10", 10, 0),
        build if build >= 10240 => ("Windows 10", 10, 0),
        build if build >= 9600 => ("Windows 8.1", 6, 3),
        build if build >= 9200 => ("Windows 8", 6, 2),
        build if build >= 7600 => ("Windows 7", 6, 1),
        build if build >= 6000 => ("Windows Vista", 6, 0),
        _ => ("Windows", 5, 1),
    }
}
```

`src/cli/commands/d/db.rs`:

```rs
//! `db` - byte + ASCII display. Renders 16 bytes per line by default
//! as `<line_va>  XX XX ... XX-XX ... XX  aaaaaaaaaaaaaaaa`.

use std::io::Write;

use vmi::{Va, VmiRead, arch::amd64::Amd64};

use crate::cli::{engine::Engine, format::FormatVa};

/// Number of bytes printed per line. Lines shorter than this are
/// padded in the hex column so the ASCII column stays aligned.
const LINE_BYTES: usize = 16;

/// Renders one `db` line.
pub fn format_line<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    _engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    line_va: Va,
    data: &[u8],
    units: usize,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    write!(w, "{}  ", FormatVa(line_va))?;

    // The 8-byte split uses '-' between positions 7 and 8.
    for i in 0..LINE_BYTES {
        let sep = match i {
            0 => "",
            8 => "-",
            _ => " ",
        };
        write!(w, "{sep}")?;
        match data.get(i) {
            Some(byte) => write!(w, "{byte:02x}")?,
            None => write!(w, "  ")?,
        }
    }

    write!(w, "  ")?;
    for &byte in &data[..units] {
        let ch = match byte {
            0x20..=0x7e => byte as char,
            _ => '.',
        };
        write!(w, "{ch}")?;
    }
    writeln!(w)
}

```

`src/cli/commands/d/dd.rs`:

```rs
//! `dd` - dword display. 4 dwords per line without symbols, 1 per
//! line when symbols are requested (the future `dds` command).

use std::io::Write;

use vmi::{Va, VmiRead, arch::amd64::Amd64};

use crate::cli::{
    engine::Engine,
    format::{FormatSymbol, FormatVa},
};

/// Byte width of one dword.
const UNIT_SIZE: usize = 4;

/// Renders one `dd` or `dds` line.
pub fn format_line<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    line_va: Va,
    data: &[u8],
    units: usize,
    show_symbols: bool,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    write!(w, "{}  ", FormatVa(line_va))?;

    for i in 0..units {
        let offset = i * UNIT_SIZE;
        let value = u32::from_le_bytes(
            data[offset..offset + UNIT_SIZE]
                .try_into()
                .expect("slice length is UNIT_SIZE by construction"),
        );
        if i > 0 {
            write!(w, " ")?;
        }
        write!(w, "{value:08x}")?;
    }

    if show_symbols && units == 1 {
        let value = u32::from_le_bytes(
            data[..UNIT_SIZE]
                .try_into()
                .expect("slice length is UNIT_SIZE by construction"),
        );
        let va = Va(value as u64);
        let vmi = engine.vmi();
        let process = engine.current_process();
        if let Ok(Some(module)) = engine.ephemera().lookup_module(vmi, process, va) {
            let symbol = engine.ephemera().resolve_symbol(vmi, &module, va);
            if !symbol.function_name.is_empty() || !symbol.module_name.is_empty() {
                write!(w, " {}", FormatSymbol(&symbol))?;
            }
        }
    }

    writeln!(w)
}
```

```rs
use std::io::Write;

/// Renders one `dq` or `dqs` / `dps` line.

    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    line_va: Va,
    data: &[u8],
    units: usize,
    show_symbols: bool,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    write!(w, "{}  ", FormatVa(line_va))?;

    for i in 0..units {
        let offset = i * UNIT_SIZE;
        let value = u64::from_le_bytes(
            data[offset..offset + UNIT_SIZE]
                .try_into()
                .expect("slice length is UNIT_SIZE by construction"),
        );
        if i > 0 {
            write!(w, " ")?;
        }
        write!(w, "{}", FormatVa(Va(value)))?;
    }

    if show_symbols && units == 1 {
        let value = u64::from_le_bytes(
            data[..UNIT_SIZE]
                .try_into()
                .expect("slice length is UNIT_SIZE by construction"),
        );
        let va = Va(value);

                write!(w, " {}", FormatSymbol(&symbol))?;

        }
    }

    writeln!(w)
}
```

`src/cli/commands/d/mod.rs`:

```rs
//! Memory-display commands. Shared IR types, runner, and format
//! dispatch live here. Individual formats (`db`, `dd`, `dq`) own
//! their line-rendering code in submodules.

mod db;
mod dd;
mod dq;

use std::io::Write;

use ephemera::ModuleEntry;
use vmi::{Va, VmiRead, arch::amd64::Amd64};

use super::HelpEntry;
use crate::cli::{
    commands::r::Register,
    engine::Engine,
    format::{FormatModuleName, FormatVa},
    repl::ReplError,
};

/// Address expression produced by the parser and consumed by
/// `eval_addr` at dispatch time.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum AddrExpr {
    /// Literal integer, already normalised (backticks stripped).
    Number(u64),

    /// Register read from the current target's register file.
    Register(Register),

    /// `module!name`. Empty modules are substituted with `nt` at
    /// parse time. Resolution happens at evaluation.
    Symbol(String),

    /// Left + right, wrapping arithmetic.
    Add(Box<AddrExpr>, Box<AddrExpr>),

    /// Left - right, wrapping arithmetic.
    Sub(Box<AddrExpr>, Box<AddrExpr>),
}

/// Selected `d*` sub-command plus per-variant flags.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum DFormat {
    /// `db`: bytes + ASCII.
    Db,

    /// `dd`: dwords. `show_symbols` routes through the `dds`
    /// one-per-line layout with a trailing symbol column.
    Dd { show_symbols: bool },

    /// `dq`: qwords. `show_symbols` is the `dqs` / `dps` layout.
    Dq { show_symbols: bool },
}

/// Parsed form of the `[Range]` argument. End addresses are inclusive
/// of the unit that contains them.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum Range {
    /// Single address, default per-format count.
    Single(AddrExpr),

    /// `L<Count>` units starting at the address.
    Count(AddrExpr, u32),

    /// `Address1 Address2`, inclusive end.
    End(AddrExpr, AddrExpr),
}

impl DFormat {
    /// Byte width of one display unit.
    fn unit_size(self) -> usize {
        match self {
            DFormat::Db => 1,
            DFormat::Dd { .. } => 4,
            DFormat::Dq { .. } => 8,
        }
    }

    /// Units printed per output line.
    fn units_per_line(self) -> usize {
        match self {
            DFormat::Db => 16,
            DFormat::Dd {
                show_symbols: false,
            } => 4,
            DFormat::Dd { show_symbols: true } => 1,
            DFormat::Dq {
                show_symbols: false,
            } => 2,
            DFormat::Dq { show_symbols: true } => 1,
        }
    }

    /// Default unit count when `[Range]` is a bare address.
    fn default_count(self) -> u32 {
        match self {
            DFormat::Db => 128,
            DFormat::Dd { .. } => 32,
            DFormat::Dq { .. } => 16,
        }
    }

    /// Renders one line. `data` is guaranteed to be `units *
    /// unit_size()` bytes long.
    fn format_line<Driver>(
        self,
        w: &mut dyn Write,
        engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
        line_va: Va,
        data: &[u8],
        units: usize,
    ) -> std::io::Result<()>
    where
        Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
    {
        match self {
            DFormat::Db => db::format_line(w, engine, line_va, data, units),
            DFormat::Dd { show_symbols } => {
                dd::format_line(w, engine, line_va, data, units, show_symbols)
            }
            DFormat::Dq { show_symbols } => {
                dq::format_line(w, engine, line_va, data, units, show_symbols)
            }
        }
    }
}

/// Help text for the `d*` commands. Extended as new formats ship.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "db  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]",
        summary: "Display memory as bytes and ASCII.",
        extra: &[
            "Address: hex, 0n<decimal>, register, or module!symbol.",
            "         Arithmetic: a+b, a-b. Empty module means nt.",
        ],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "dd  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]",
        summary: "Display memory as DWORDs.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "dq  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]",
        summary: "Display memory as QWORDs.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "dp  [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]",
        summary: "Alias for dq on 64-bit.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "dps [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]",
        summary: "Display memory as QWORDs with symbols.",
        extra: &[],
    },
];

/// Resolves an [`AddrExpr`] to a concrete virtual address.
fn eval_addr<Driver>(engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>, expr: &AddrExpr) -> Result<Va, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    match expr {
        AddrExpr::Number(value) => Ok(Va(*value)),
        AddrExpr::Register(register) => read_register_addr(engine, *register),
        AddrExpr::Symbol(qualified) => resolve_symbol_addr(engine, qualified),
        AddrExpr::Add(lhs, rhs) => Ok(Va(eval_addr(engine, lhs)?
            .0
            .wrapping_add(eval_addr(engine, rhs)?.0))),
        AddrExpr::Sub(lhs, rhs) => Ok(Va(eval_addr(engine, lhs)?
            .0
            .wrapping_sub(eval_addr(engine, rhs)?.0))),
    }
}

/// Reads a register as a 64-bit virtual address. Segment selectors
/// and `efl` are rejected.
fn read_register_addr<Driver>(
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    register: Register,
) -> Result<Va, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let registers = engine.vmi().registers();
    let value = match register {
        Register::Rax => registers.rax,
        Register::Rbx => registers.rbx,
        Register::Rcx => registers.rcx,
        Register::Rdx => registers.rdx,
        Register::Rsi => registers.rsi,
        Register::Rdi => registers.rdi,
        Register::Rbp => registers.rbp,
        Register::Rsp => registers.rsp,
        Register::R8 => registers.r8,
        Register::R9 => registers.r9,
        Register::R10 => registers.r10,
        Register::R11 => registers.r11,
        Register::R12 => registers.r12,
        Register::R13 => registers.r13,
        Register::R14 => registers.r14,
        Register::R15 => registers.r15,
        Register::Rip => registers.rip,
        other => {
            return Err(ReplError::BadAddress(format!(
                "{other:?} is not an address register"
            )));
        }
    };
    Ok(Va(value))
}

/// Resolves a `module!name` string to an address. Only the kernel
/// module (`nt`) is supported.
fn resolve_symbol_addr<Driver>(
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    qualified: &str,
) -> Result<Va, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let (module_name, symbol_name) = match qualified.split_once('!') {
        Some(pair) => pair,
        None => return Err(ReplError::SymbolNotFound(qualified.to_string())),
    };

    let module = match find_kernel_module_by_display_name(engine, module_name)? {
        Some(module) => module,
        None => return Err(ReplError::SymbolNotFound(qualified.to_string())),
    };

    let base = module.base_address();

    let rva = match module_name.eq_ignore_ascii_case("nt") {
        true => match engine.profile().find_symbol(symbol_name) {
            Some(rva) => rva,
            None => return Err(ReplError::SymbolNotFound(qualified.to_string())),
        },
        false => return Err(ReplError::SymbolNotFound(qualified.to_string())),
    };

    Ok(Va(base.0.wrapping_add(rva)))
}

/// Finds the kernel module whose display name (per
/// [`FormatModuleName`]) matches `display_name` case-insensitively.
fn find_kernel_module_by_display_name<Driver>(
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    display_name: &str,
) -> Result<Option<ModuleEntry>, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    for module in vmi.os().modules()? {
        let module = match module {
            Ok(module) => module,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "skipping unreadable kernel module");
                continue;
            }
        };
        let entry = match ModuleEntry::try_from(module) {
            Ok(entry) => entry,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "skipping module, ModuleEntry conversion failed");
                continue;
            }
        };
        let rendered = FormatModuleName(entry.name()).to_string();
        if rendered.eq_ignore_ascii_case(display_name) {
            return Ok(Some(entry));
        }
    }
    Ok(None)
}

/// Entry point called by dispatch for `Command::D`.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    format: DFormat,
    range: Range,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let (start, unit_count) = resolve_range(engine, format, &range)?;
    if unit_count == 0 {
        return Ok(());
    }

    let unit_size = format.unit_size();
    let units_per_line = format.units_per_line();
    let line_count = unit_count.div_ceil(units_per_line);

    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let mut scratch = vec![0u8; units_per_line * unit_size];

    for line_idx in 0..line_count {
        let units_on_line = (unit_count - line_idx * units_per_line).min(units_per_line);
        let bytes_on_line = units_on_line * unit_size;
        let line_va = Va(start
            .0
            .wrapping_add((line_idx * units_per_line * unit_size) as u64));

        let buf = &mut scratch[..bytes_on_line];
        match vmi.read(line_va, buf) {
            Ok(()) => format.format_line(w, engine, line_va, buf, units_on_line)?,
            Err(err) => writeln!(w, "{}  ?? read failed: {err}", FormatVa(line_va))?,
        }

        engine.check_interrupt()?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Lowers [`Range`] to a concrete `(start, unit_count)` pair.
fn resolve_range<Driver>(
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    format: DFormat,
    range: &Range,
) -> Result<(Va, usize), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let unit_size = format.unit_size() as u64;
    match range {
        Range::Single(expr) => {
            let start = eval_addr(engine, expr)?;
            Ok((start, format.default_count() as usize))
        }
        Range::Count(expr, count) => {
            let start = eval_addr(engine, expr)?;
            Ok((start, *count as usize))
        }
        Range::End(lhs, rhs) => {
            let start = eval_addr(engine, lhs)?;
            let end = eval_addr(engine, rhs)?;
            if end.0 < start.0 {
                return Ok((start, 0));
            }
            let span = end.0 - start.0;
            let units = usize::try_from(span / unit_size)
                .unwrap_or(usize::MAX - 1)
                .saturating_add(1);
            Ok((start, units))
        }
    }
}
```

`src/cli/commands/dt.rs`:

```rs
//! Display type command (`dt`).
//!
//! Produces WinDbg-like output showing a struct type's layout,
//! and optionally reads memory at a given address to display field values.

use std::io::Write;

use isr::{
    Profile,
    visit::{FieldValue, FieldValueKind, visit_struct, visit_struct_schema},
};
use vmi::{
    Va, VmiRead, VmiState,
    arch::amd64::Amd64,
    os::windows::{WindowsOs, WindowsOsExt as _},
};

use crate::cli::{
    commands::HelpEntry,
    engine::Engine,
    format::{FormatSymbol, FormatVa},
    repl::ReplError,
};

/// Help text for `dt`.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[HelpEntry {
    syntax: "dt <type> [address]",
    summary: "Display type layout, optionally at an address.",
    extra: &[],
}];

/// Runs the `dt` (display type) command.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    profile: &Profile,
    type_name: &str,
    address: Option<Va>,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let struct_def = match profile.find_struct(type_name) {
        Some(s) => s,
        None => {
            writeln!(w, "Symbol {type_name} not found")?;
            return Ok(());
        }
    };

    writeln!(w, "nt!{type_name}")?;

    if let Some(addr) = address {
        let vmi = engine.vmi();
        let mut buf = vec![0u8; struct_def.size() as usize];
        match vmi.read(addr, &mut buf) {
            Ok(()) => {
                visit_struct(
                    profile,
                    &struct_def,
                    |field| {
                        let field_va = Va(addr.0 + field.offset as u64);
                        write!(w, "   +0x{:03x} {:<20}: ", field.offset, field.name)?;
                        print_variant(w, engine, &field.value, field_va)?;
                        writeln!(w)
                    },
                    &buf,
                )?;
            }
            Err(err) => {
                writeln!(w, "Memory read error at {}: {err}", FormatVa(addr))?;
            }
        }
    }
    else {
        visit_struct_schema(profile, struct_def, |field| {
            write!(w, "   +0x{:03x} {:<20}: ", field.offset, field.name)?;
            print_variant_kind(w, &field.value)?;
            writeln!(w)
        })?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Prints a `VariantKind` as a WinDbg-style type description.
fn print_variant_kind(w: &mut dyn Write, kind: &FieldValueKind) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    match kind {
        FieldValueKind::Void => write!(w, "Void"),
        FieldValueKind::Bool => write!(w, "Bool"),
        FieldValueKind::Char8 | FieldValueKind::I8 => write!(w, "Char"),
        FieldValueKind::Char16 => write!(w, "Wchar"),
        FieldValueKind::Char32 => write!(w, "Char32"),
        FieldValueKind::U8 => write!(w, "UChar"),
        FieldValueKind::I16 => write!(w, "Int2B"),
        FieldValueKind::U16 => write!(w, "Uint2B"),
        FieldValueKind::I32 => write!(w, "Int4B"),
        FieldValueKind::U32 => write!(w, "Uint4B"),
        FieldValueKind::I64 => write!(w, "Int8B"),
        FieldValueKind::U64 => write!(w, "Uint8B"),
        FieldValueKind::I128 => write!(w, "Int16B"),
        FieldValueKind::U128 => write!(w, "Uint16B"),
        FieldValueKind::F32 => write!(w, "Float"),
        FieldValueKind::F64 => write!(w, "Double"),
        FieldValueKind::F8 | FieldValueKind::F16 | FieldValueKind::F128 => write!(w, "Float"),
        FieldValueKind::Struct { type_name, .. } => write!(w, "{type_name}"),
        FieldValueKind::Enum { type_name, .. } => write!(w, "{type_name}"),
        FieldValueKind::Pointer { subtype, size } => {
            write!(w, "Ptr{} ", *size * 8)?;
            print_variant_kind(w, subtype)
        }
        FieldValueKind::Array { subtype, dims, .. } => {
            for dim in dims {
                write!(w, "[{dim}]")?;
            }
            write!(w, " ")?;
            print_variant_kind(w, subtype)
        }
        FieldValueKind::Bitfield {
            bit_position,
            bit_length,
            ..
        } => {
            write!(
                w,
                "Pos {bit_position}, {bit_length} Bit{}",
                if *bit_length > 1 { "s" } else { "" }
            )
        }
        FieldValueKind::Function => write!(w, "Function"),
    }
}

/// Formats a `Variant` produced by `isrdump_struct` in WinDbg style.
///
/// `va` is the virtual address of the field being displayed, used to
/// dereference well-known embedded structs like `_UNICODE_STRING`.
fn print_variant<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    variant: &FieldValue,
    va: Va,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    match variant {
        FieldValue::Void => write!(w, "Void"),
        FieldValue::Bool(v) => write!(w, "{}", if *v { "true" } else { "false" }),

        FieldValue::Char8(v) | FieldValue::U8(v) => {
            if *v == 0 {
                write!(w, "0 ''")
            }
            else if v.is_ascii_graphic() {
                write!(w, "0x{v:x} '{}'", *v as char)
            }
            else {
                write!(w, "0x{v:x} ''")
            }
        }
        FieldValue::Char16(v) | FieldValue::U16(v) => print_hex_u32(w, *v as u32),
        FieldValue::Char32(v) | FieldValue::U32(v) => print_hex_u32(w, *v),
        FieldValue::U64(v) => print_hex_u64(w, *v),
        FieldValue::U128(v) => print_hex_u64(w, *v as u64),

        FieldValue::I8(v) => write!(w, "0n{v}"),
        FieldValue::I16(v) => write!(w, "0n{v}"),
        FieldValue::I32(v) => write!(w, "0n{v}"),
        FieldValue::I64(v) => write!(w, "0n{v}"),
        FieldValue::I128(v) => write!(w, "0n{v}"),

        FieldValue::F8(v) => write!(w, "0x{v:x}"),
        FieldValue::F16(v) => write!(w, "0x{v:x}"),
        FieldValue::F32(v) => write!(w, "{v}"),
        FieldValue::F64(v) => write!(w, "{v}"),
        FieldValue::F128(v) => write!(w, "0x{v:x}"),

        FieldValue::Enum {
            type_name, value, ..
        } => {
            if *value == 0 {
                write!(w, "0 ({type_name})")
            }
            else {
                write!(w, "0x{value:x} ({type_name})")
            }
        }

        FieldValue::Struct {
            type_name, data, ..
        } => print_struct_value(w, &engine.vmi(), data, type_name, va),

        FieldValue::Pointer {
            subtype,
            size,
            value,
        } => print_pointer_value(w, engine, Va(*value), *size, subtype.as_ref()),

        FieldValue::Array {
            subtype,
            dims,
            data,
            ..
        } => print_array_value(w, engine, data, dims, subtype.as_ref(), va),

        FieldValue::Bitfield {
            bit_position,
            bit_length,
            value,
            ..
        } => {
            let mask = if *bit_length >= 64 {
                u64::MAX
            }
            else {
                (1u64 << bit_length) - 1
            };
            let val = (value >> bit_position) & mask;
            write!(w, "0y{:0width$b}", val, width = *bit_length as usize)
        }

        FieldValue::Function { value } => {
            if *value == 0 {
                write!(w, "(null) ")
            }
            else {
                print_hex_u64(w, *value)
            }
        }
    }
}

fn print_hex_u32(w: &mut dyn Write, val: u32) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    if val == 0 {
        write!(w, "0")
    }
    else {
        write!(w, "0x{val:x}")
    }
}

fn print_hex_u64(w: &mut dyn Write, val: u64) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    if val == 0 {
        write!(w, "0")
    }
    else if val <= 0xFFFF_FFFF {
        write!(w, "0x{val:x}")
    }
    else {
        write!(w, "0x{}", FormatVa(Va(val)))
    }
}

/// Prints an embedded struct value with special formatting for well-known
/// types (matching WinDbg's `DumpKnownStructFormat` in dbgeng.dll).
fn print_struct_value<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    vmi: &VmiState<'_, WindowsOs<Driver>>,
    data: &[u8],
    type_name: &str,
    va: Va,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    match type_name {
        "_UNICODE_STRING" => {
            write!(w, "{type_name}")?;
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.os().read_unicode_string(va) {
                write!(w, " \"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        "_ANSI_STRING" | "_STRING" => {
            write!(w, "{type_name}")?;
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.os().read_ansi_string(va) {
                write!(w, " \"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        "_GUID" if data.len() >= 16 => {
            let d1 = u32::from_le_bytes(data[0..4].try_into().unwrap());
            let d2 = u16::from_le_bytes(data[4..6].try_into().unwrap());
            let d3 = u16::from_le_bytes(data[6..8].try_into().unwrap());
            let d4 = &data[8..16];
            write!(
                w,
                "{{{d1:08x}-{d2:04x}-{d3:04x}-{:02x}{:02x}-{:02x}{:02x}{:02x}{:02x}{:02x}{:02x}}}",
                d4[0], d4[1], d4[2], d4[3], d4[4], d4[5], d4[6], d4[7],
            )?;
        }
        "_LIST_ENTRY" if data.len() >= 16 => {
            write!(w, "{type_name}")?;
            let flink = u64::from_le_bytes(data[0..8].try_into().unwrap());
            let blink = u64::from_le_bytes(data[8..16].try_into().unwrap());
            write!(
                w,
                " [ 0x{} - 0x{} ]",
                FormatVa(Va(flink)),
                FormatVa(Va(blink))
            )?;
        }
        "_SINGLE_LIST_ENTRY" if data.len() >= 8 => {
            write!(w, "{type_name}")?;
            let next = u64::from_le_bytes(data[0..8].try_into().unwrap());
            if next == 0 {
                write!(w, " [(null)]")?;
            }
            else {
                write!(w, " [0x{}]", FormatVa(Va(next)))?;
            }
        }
        "_LARGE_INTEGER" | "_ULARGE_INTEGER" => {
            let val = u64::from_le_bytes(data[0..8].try_into().unwrap());
            write!(w, "{type_name} 0x{}", FormatVa(Va(val)))?;
        }
        "_FILETIME" => {
            let val = u64::from_le_bytes(data[0..8].try_into().unwrap());
            write!(w, "{type_name} 0x{}", FormatVa(Va(val)))?;
            if val != 0
                && let Some(s) = filetime_to_string(val)
            {
                write!(w, " ({s})")?;
            }
        }
        _ => {
            write!(w, "{type_name}")?;
        }
    }
    Ok(())
}

/// Prints a pointer value. Dereferences char/wchar pointers to show
/// string content, dereferences well-known string structs, and resolves
/// function pointers to symbols.
fn print_pointer_value<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    value: Va,
    size: u64,
    subtype: &FieldValueKind,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    if value.is_null() {
        return write!(w, "(null) ");
    }

    if size == 8 {
        write!(w, "0x{}", FormatVa(value))?;
    }
    else {
        write!(w, "0x{:08x}", value.0)?;
    }

    let vmi = engine.vmi();

    match subtype {
        FieldValueKind::Char8 | FieldValueKind::I8 | FieldValueKind::U8 => {
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.read_string_limited(value, 256) {
                write!(w, "  \"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        FieldValueKind::Char16 => {
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.read_string_utf16_limited(value, 256) {
                write!(w, "  \"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        FieldValueKind::Struct { type_name, .. } if *type_name == "_UNICODE_STRING" => {
            write!(w, " {type_name}")?;
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.os().read_unicode_string(value) {
                write!(w, " \"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        FieldValueKind::Struct { type_name, .. }
            if matches!(*type_name, "_ANSI_STRING" | "_STRING") =>
        {
            write!(w, " {type_name}")?;
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.os().read_ansi_string(value) {
                write!(w, " \"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        FieldValueKind::Function => {
            let process = engine.current_process();
            if let Ok(Some(module)) = engine.ephemera().lookup_module(vmi, process, value) {
                let symbol = engine.ephemera().resolve_symbol(vmi, &module, value);
                write!(w, " {}", FormatSymbol(&symbol))?;
            }
        }
        kind => {
            write!(w, " ")?;
            print_variant_kind(w, kind)?;
        }
    }
    Ok(())
}

fn print_array_value<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    data: &[u8],
    dims: &[u64],
    subtype: &FieldValueKind,
    va: Va,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();

    for dim in dims {
        write!(w, "[{dim}]")?;
    }
    write!(w, " ")?;

    let count = dims.iter().product::<u64>() as usize;

    match subtype {
        FieldValueKind::Char8 | FieldValueKind::U8 => {
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.read_string_limited(va, count) {
                write!(w, "\"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        FieldValueKind::Char16 | FieldValueKind::U16 => {
            if let Ok(s) = vmi.read_string_utf16_limited(va, count * 2) {
                write!(w, "\"{s}\"")?;
            }
        }
        _ => {
            let elem_size = subtype.size() as usize;
            if elem_size > 0 && elem_size <= data.len() {
                let val = read_uint_le(data, elem_size);
                if val == 0 {
                    write!(w, "0")?;
                }
                else {
                    write!(w, "0x{val:x}")?;
                    // Resolve symbol for function pointer arrays.
                    if let FieldValueKind::Pointer { subtype, .. } = subtype
                        && matches!(subtype.as_ref(), FieldValueKind::Function)
                    {
                        let vmi = engine.vmi();
                        let process = engine.current_process();
                        if let Ok(Some(module)) =
                            engine.ephemera().lookup_module(vmi, process, Va(val))
                        {
                            let sym = engine.ephemera().resolve_symbol(vmi, &module, Va(val));
                            write!(w, " {}", FormatSymbol(&sym))?;
                        }
                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }
    Ok(())
}

fn read_uint_le(data: &[u8], size: usize) -> u64 {
    match size {
        1 => data[0] as u64,
        2 => u16::from_le_bytes(data[..2].try_into().unwrap()) as u64,
        4 => u32::from_le_bytes(data[..4].try_into().unwrap()) as u64,
        8 => u64::from_le_bytes(data[..8].try_into().unwrap()),
        _ => 0,
    }
}

/// Converts a Windows FILETIME (100-ns intervals since 1601-01-01) to a
/// human-readable `HH:MM:SS MM/DD/YYYY` string.
fn filetime_to_string(filetime: u64) -> Option<String> {
    const EPOCH_DIFF: u64 = 116_444_736_000_000_000;

    let unix_100ns = filetime.checked_sub(EPOCH_DIFF)?;
    let unix_secs = (unix_100ns / 10_000_000) as i64;

    let mut remaining = unix_secs;
    let secs = (remaining.rem_euclid(60)) as u32;
    remaining = remaining.div_euclid(60);
    let mins = (remaining.rem_euclid(60)) as u32;
    remaining = remaining.div_euclid(60);
    let hours = (remaining.rem_euclid(24)) as u32;
    let mut days = remaining.div_euclid(24);

    days += 719_468;
    let era = days.div_euclid(146_097);
    let doe = days.rem_euclid(146_097) as u32;
    let yoe = (doe - doe / 1460 + doe / 36524 - doe / 146096) / 365;
    let y = (yoe as i64) + era * 400;
    let doy = doe - (365 * yoe + yoe / 4 - yoe / 100);
    let mp = (5 * doy + 2) / 153;
    let d = doy - (153 * mp + 2) / 5 + 1;
    let m = if mp < 10 { mp + 3 } else { mp - 9 };
    let y = if m <= 2 { y + 1 } else { y };

    Some(format!(
        "{hours:02}:{mins:02}:{secs:02} {m:02}/{d:02}/{y:04}"
    ))
}

#[cfg(test)]
mod tests {
    use super::*;

    #[test]
    fn test_filetime_to_string() {
        assert_eq!(
            filetime_to_string(0x01db5125_231cc195),
            Some("08:16:28 12/18/2024".to_string()),
        );
        assert_eq!(filetime_to_string(0), None);
        assert_eq!(
            filetime_to_string(116_444_736_000_000_000),
            Some("00:00:00 01/01/1970".to_string()),
        );
    }
}
```

`src/cli/commands/k.rs`:

```rs
//! Stack backtrace command.
//!
//! Walks the call stack using PE unwind information and prints one
//! of four WinDbg-compatible layouts: `k`, `kb`, `kc`, `kv`.

use std::io::Write;

use ephemera::{ResolvedSymbol, UnwindTarget, WalkFrame};
use vmi::{Va, VmiRead, arch::amd64::Amd64};

use crate::cli::{
    commands::HelpEntry,
    engine::Engine,
    format::{FormatSymbol, FormatVa},
    repl::ReplError,
};

/// Help text for `k`, `kb`, `kc`, `kv`.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "k  [FrameCount]",
        summary: "Display stack backtrace: Child-SP, RetAddr, Call Site.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "kb [FrameCount]",
        summary: "As k, plus the first four home-space args per frame.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "kc [FrameCount]",
        summary: "As k, Call Site only.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "kv [FrameCount]",
        summary: "As kb, plus TrapFrame @ addr for trap-handler frames.",
        extra: &[],
    },
];

/// Column layout variant for `k`.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum KMode {
    /// `k`: `# Child-SP RetAddr Call Site`.
    K,

    /// `kb`: `# RetAddr : Args to Child : Call Site`.
    Kb,

    /// `kc`: `# Call Site`.
    Kc,

    /// `kv`: `# Child-SP RetAddr : Args to Child : Call Site [(TrapFrame @ addr)]`.
    Kv,
}

impl KMode {
    /// Parses the mode suffix of `k`. The empty string and the single
    /// letters `b`, `c`, `v` are accepted. Other strings return `None`.
    pub fn parse(suffix: &str) -> Option<Self> {
        match suffix {
            "" => Some(Self::K),
            "b" => Some(Self::Kb),
            "c" => Some(Self::Kc),
            "v" => Some(Self::Kv),
            _ => None,
        }
    }

    /// Returns true if Child-SP is printed.
    fn has_child_sp(self) -> bool {
        matches!(self, KMode::K | KMode::Kv)
    }

    /// Returns true if RetAddr is printed.
    fn has_ret_addr(self) -> bool {
        matches!(self, KMode::K | KMode::Kb | KMode::Kv)
    }

    /// Returns true if the four argument home-space slots are printed.
    fn has_params(self) -> bool {
        matches!(self, KMode::Kb | KMode::Kv)
    }

    /// Returns true if the `(TrapFrame @ <addr>)` annotation is printed
    /// for trap-handler frames.
    fn has_trap_annotation(self) -> bool {
        matches!(self, KMode::Kv)
    }
}

/// Runs `k`, `kb`, `kc`, or `kv` with an optional frame cap.
///
/// `show_numbers` controls whether a leading `NN` frame-number column
/// is printed. The REPL passes `true`. `!thread` passes `false` to
/// match WinDbg's `!thread` stack, which omits the column.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    target: &UnwindTarget,
    mode: KMode,
    frame_count: Option<u32>,
    show_numbers: bool,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    print_header(w, mode, show_numbers)?;

    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let session = engine.ephemera();
    let process_object = target.process_object;

    let cap = frame_count
        .map(|frame_count| frame_count as usize)
        .unwrap_or(usize::MAX);

    for (number, frame) in ephemera::walk_stack(vmi, session, target.clone())
        .take(cap)
        .enumerate()
    {
        engine.check_interrupt()?;

        let frame = match frame {
            Ok(frame) => frame,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "unwind failed");
                break;
            }
        };

        let call_site = match session.lookup_module(vmi, process_object, frame.call_site)? {
            Some(call_site) => session.resolve_symbol(vmi, &call_site, frame.call_site),
            None => ResolvedSymbol {
                module_name: String::new(),
                function_name: String::new(),
                offset: frame.call_site.0,
            },
        };

        print_frame(w, number, &frame, &call_site, mode, show_numbers)?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Prints the column header for `mode`.
fn print_header(w: &mut dyn Write, mode: KMode, show_numbers: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let mut cols = Vec::new();
    if show_numbers {
        cols.push(" #".to_string());
    }
    if mode.has_child_sp() {
        cols.push(format!("{:<18}", "Child-SP"));
    }
    if mode.has_ret_addr() {
        cols.push(format!("{:<20}", "RetAddr"));
    }
    if mode.has_params() {
        cols.push(format!(": {:<71}", "Args to Child"));
        cols.push(":".to_string());
    }
    cols.push("Call Site".to_string());
    writeln!(w, "{}", cols.join(" "))
}

/// Prints one frame row using `mode`'s column layout.
fn print_frame(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    number: usize,
    frame: &WalkFrame,
    call_site: &ResolvedSymbol,
    mode: KMode,
    show_numbers: bool,
) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let mut cols = Vec::new();
    if show_numbers {
        cols.push(format!("{number:02x}"));
    }
    if mode.has_child_sp() {
        cols.push(format!("{}", FormatVa(frame.child_sp)));
    }
    if mode.has_ret_addr() {
        cols.push(format!("{}", FormatVa(frame.frame.instruction_pointer)));
    }
    if mode.has_params() {
        let params = frame.frame.params;
        cols.push(format!(
            ": {} {} {} {} :",
            FormatVa(Va(params[0])),
            FormatVa(Va(params[1])),
            FormatVa(Va(params[2])),
            FormatVa(Va(params[3])),
        ));
    }
    cols.push(format!("{}", FormatSymbol(call_site)));
    let mut row = cols.join(" ");
    if mode.has_trap_annotation() && frame.frame.machine_frame {
        row.push_str(&format!(" (TrapFrame @ {})", FormatVa(frame.child_sp)));
    }
    writeln!(w, "{row}")
}
```
