`src/cli/commands/process.rs`:

```rs
//! `!process` command handler.
//!
//! Mirrors WinDbg's `!process [Process [Flags [Image]]]`. See the
//! canonical Microsoft Learn page for flag semantics.

use std::io::Write;

use vmi::{
    Va, VmiRead, VmiVa as _,
    arch::amd64::Amd64,
    os::{ProcessObject, VmiOsProcess as _, VmiOsThread as _, windows::WindowsProcess},
};

use crate::cli::{
    commands::{HelpEntry, thread::ThreadFlags},
    engine::Engine,
    output::IndentWriter,
    repl::ReplError,
};

/// Help text for `!process`.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[HelpEntry {
    syntax: "!process [Proc [Flags [Image]]]",
    summary: "Information about a process or all processes.",
    extra: &["Proc: PID, EPROCESS addr, 0 (all), -1 (current)."],
}];

/// Target selector for `!process`.
///
/// The WinDbg `Process` argument is a single hex value that can mean
/// "address", "PID", "all", or "current" depending on magnitude and
/// literal form. Disambiguation happens at parse time.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum ProcessTarget {
    /// No `Process` argument supplied.
    Default,

    /// Literal `-1`, the currently executing process.
    Current,

    /// Literal `0`, every active process.
    All,

    /// Small hex value (<= `u32::MAX`), interpreted as a process ID.
    Pid(u32),

    /// Hex value above `u32::MAX`, interpreted as an EPROCESS VA.
    Address(u64),
}

impl ProcessTarget {
    /// Returns WinDbg's documented default flag bitmask for this
    /// target: `0x03` when the target is omitted, `0`, or `-1`; `0x0f`
    /// when a specific process is named.
    pub fn default_flags(&self) -> ProcessFlags {
        match self {
            Self::Default | Self::Current | Self::All => ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x03),
            Self::Pid(_) | Self::Address(_) => ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x0f),
        }
    }
}

bitflags::bitflags! {
    /// WinDbg `!process` flag bitmask. Unknown bits are preserved but
    /// ignored, mirroring WinDbg's permissive parsing.
    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
    pub struct ProcessFlags: u64 {
        /// Time and priority statistics.
        const TIME           = 0x01;

        /// Thread list with wait states. Combined with [`Self::THREADS`]
        /// each thread is shown with a stack trace.
        const THREADS_WAIT   = 0x02;

        /// Thread list, one line per thread.
        const THREADS        = 0x04;

        /// Return address and stack pointer per frame, no arguments.
        const STACK_NOARGS   = 0x08;

        /// Set the process context to each walked process.
        const SWITCH_CONTEXT = 0x10;
    }
}

/// Display options derived from the WinDbg flag bitmask.
struct Display {
    /// Show a thread list under each process block.
    show_threads: bool,

    /// Show a stack trace under each thread. Requires `show_threads`.
    show_stacks: bool,

    /// Omit per-frame arguments from the stack trace.
    show_noargs: bool,

    /// Switch the process context for stack unwinding.
    switch_context: bool,

    /// Include the `VadRoot` line in the process header. Gated on the
    /// WinDbg `TIME` bit, which also gates the larger statistics block
    /// that ephemera does not yet render.
    show_vad_root: bool,
}

impl Display {
    /// Decodes the relevant bits out of the WinDbg flag bitmask.
    ///
    /// `THREADS_WAIT | THREADS` together request per-thread stacks.
    /// Either one alone requests the thread list with no stacks.
    fn from_flags(flags: ProcessFlags) -> Self {
        let thread_bits = ProcessFlags::THREADS_WAIT | ProcessFlags::THREADS;
        Self {
            show_threads: flags.intersects(thread_bits),
            show_stacks: flags.contains(thread_bits),
            show_noargs: flags.contains(ProcessFlags::STACK_NOARGS),
            switch_context: flags.contains(ProcessFlags::SWITCH_CONTEXT),
            show_vad_root: flags.contains(ProcessFlags::TIME),
        }
    }
}

/// Runs `!process` with a fully parsed target.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    target: ProcessTarget,
    flags: ProcessFlags,
    image: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let display = Display::from_flags(flags);

    match target {
        ProcessTarget::Default | ProcessTarget::Current => {
            let process = engine.current_process();
            print_one(w, engine, process, &display)?;
        }
        ProcessTarget::All => {
            print_all(w, engine, &display, image)?;
        }
        ProcessTarget::Pid(pid) => {
            let process = find_by_pid(engine, pid)?;
            print_one(w, engine, process, &display)?;
        }
        ProcessTarget::Address(va) => {
            print_one(w, engine, ProcessObject(Va(va)), &display)?;
        }
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Walks every active process and prints each one that matches `image`
/// (if supplied). Respects Ctrl-C between processes.
fn print_all<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    display: &Display,
    image: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let mut processes = Vec::new();
    for process in vmi.os().processes()? {
        let process = match process {
            Ok(process) => process,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::error!(%err, "failed to read process");
                continue;
            }
        };

        if let Some(filter) = image {
            match process.name() {
                Ok(name) if name == filter => {}
                Ok(_) => continue,
                Err(err) => {
                    tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read image name for filter");
                    continue;
                }
            }
        }

        match process.object() {
            Ok(object) => processes.push(object),
            Err(err) => tracing::error!(%err, "failed to read process object"),
        }
    }

    for process in processes {
        engine.check_interrupt()?;
        print_one(w, engine, process, display)?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Prints one process block, optionally followed by a thread list and
/// per-thread stacks.
fn print_one<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    process_object: ProcessObject,
    display: &Display,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let process = vmi.os().process(process_object)?;
    print_process_header(w, &process, display)?;

    if !display.show_threads {
        return Ok(());
    }

    let mut thread_objects = Vec::new();
    for thread in process.threads()? {
        let thread = match thread {
            Ok(thread) => thread,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread");
                continue;
            }
        };
        match thread.object() {
            Ok(object) => thread_objects.push(object),
            Err(err) => tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread object"),
        }
    }

    let thread_flags = thread_flags_from_display(display);
    let had_threads = !thread_objects.is_empty();
    for thread_object in thread_objects {
        engine.check_interrupt()?;
        let mut indented = IndentWriter::new(&mut *w, 8);
        super::thread::print_block(&mut indented, engine, thread_object, thread_flags)?;
        if display.show_stacks {
            writeln!(w)?;
        }
    }
    if had_threads && !display.show_stacks {
        writeln!(w)?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Looks up a process by its PID by scanning the active process list.
fn find_by_pid<Driver>(engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>, pid: u32) -> Result<ProcessObject, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    for process in vmi.os().processes()? {
        let process = match process {
            Ok(process) => process,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read process while searching by pid");
                continue;
            }
        };
        match process.id() {
            Ok(id) if id.0 == pid => return Ok(process.object()?),
            Ok(_) => continue,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read pid while searching by pid");
                continue;
            }
        }
    }
    Err(ReplError::ProcessNotFound(pid))
}

/// Prints the process header block. Each field is read independently so
/// a single failed read does not abort the whole block. `VadRoot` only
/// renders when `display.show_vad_root` is set.
fn print_process_header<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    process: &WindowsProcess<'_, Driver>,
    display: &Display,
) -> std::io::Result<()>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let process_va = process.object_va_display();
    let session_id = process.session_id_display();
    let pid = process.pid_display();
    let parent_pid = process.parent_pid_display();
    let peb = process.peb_display();
    let translation_root = process.translation_root_display();
    let object_table = process.object_table_display();
    let image = process.image_display();

    writeln!(w, "PROCESS {process_va}")?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "    SessionId: {session_id}  Cid: {pid:<8}Peb: {peb}  ParentCid: {parent_pid}"
    )?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "    DirBase: {translation_root}  ObjectTable: {object_table}"
    )?;
    writeln!(w, "    Image: {image}")?;
    if display.show_vad_root {
        let vad_root = process.vad_root_display();
        writeln!(w, "    VadRoot {vad_root}")?;
    }
    writeln!(w)?;

    Ok(())
}

/// Converts a `!process` `Display` into a `ThreadFlags`. Bit positions
/// align 1:1 with `ProcessFlags`. The result sets `WAIT_STATE` whenever
/// threads are being rendered, plus any of `STACK`, `STACK_NOARGS`, and
/// `SWITCH_CONTEXT` that the display requests.
fn thread_flags_from_display(display: &Display) -> ThreadFlags {
    let mut flags = ThreadFlags::WAIT_STATE;
    if display.show_stacks {
        flags |= ThreadFlags::STACK;
    }
    if display.show_noargs {
        flags |= ThreadFlags::STACK_NOARGS;
    }
    if display.switch_context {
        flags |= ThreadFlags::SWITCH_CONTEXT;
    }
    flags
}

/// Adapter trait over the VMI process type, giving each printable
/// field a single method that returns a preformatted `String`. Reads
/// that fail log at debug and render as `?`. Reads that return `None`
/// render as `-`.
trait VmiOsProcessExt {
    fn object_va_display(&self) -> String;
    fn session_id_display(&self) -> String;
    fn pid_display(&self) -> String;
    fn parent_pid_display(&self) -> String;
    fn image_display(&self) -> String;
    fn peb_display(&self) -> String;
    fn translation_root_display(&self) -> String;
    fn object_table_display(&self) -> String;
    fn vad_root_display(&self) -> String;
}

impl<'a, Driver> VmiOsProcessExt for WindowsProcess<'a, Driver>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    fn object_va_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.object() {
            Ok(object) => format!("{object:x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read process object");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn session_id_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.session() {
            Ok(Some(session)) => match session.id() {
                Ok(id) => format!("{id}"),
                Err(err) => {
                    tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read session id");
                    "?".to_string()
                }
            },
            Ok(None) => "-".to_string(),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read session");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn pid_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.id() {
            Ok(pid) => format!("{pid:x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read pid");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn parent_pid_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.parent_id() {
            Ok(parent_id) => format!("{parent_id:x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read parent pid");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn image_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.name() {
            Ok(name) => name,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read image name");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn peb_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.peb() {
            Ok(Some(peb)) => format!("{:x}", peb.va()),
            Ok(None) => "-".to_string(),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read peb");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn translation_root_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.translation_root() {
            Ok(pa) => format!("{pa:x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read translation root");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn object_table_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.handle_table() {
            Ok(Some(table)) => format!("{:x}", table.va()),
            Ok(None) => "-".to_string(),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read handle table");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn vad_root_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.vad_root() {
            Ok(Some(region)) => format!("{:x}", region.va()),
            Ok(None) => "-".to_string(),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read vad root");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }
}
```

`src/cli/commands/r.rs`:

```rs
//! `r` command handler.
//!
//! Mirrors WinDbg's compact `r` register dump. Renders the GP registers,
//! the mnemonic rflags line, and the segment selectors. The trailing
//! symbol + disassembly line that WinDbg emits at RIP is not rendered.

use std::io::Write;

use vmi::{
    VmiRead,
    arch::amd64::{Amd64, Registers, Rflags},
};

use super::HelpEntry;
use crate::cli::{engine::Engine, repl::ReplError};

/// Help text for `r`.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[HelpEntry {
    syntax: "r [Reg]",
    summary: "Display registers.",
    extra: &["Reg: rax..r15, rip, rsp, rbp, cs/ds/es/fs/gs/ss, efl."],
}];

/// What `r` should render.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum RTarget {
    /// Full register dump.
    All,

    /// A single register.
    One(Register),
}

/// Register selectable via `r <name>` or `r<name>`. Only the canonical
/// 64-bit GP names, segment names, and `efl`/`rflags` are accepted.
#[allow(missing_docs)]
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum Register {
    Rax,
    Rbx,
    Rcx,
    Rdx,
    Rsi,
    Rdi,
    Rbp,
    Rsp,
    R8,
    R9,
    R10,
    R11,
    R12,
    R13,
    R14,
    R15,
    Rip,
    Cs,
    Ds,
    Es,
    Fs,
    Gs,
    Ss,
    Efl,
}

impl Register {
    /// Parses a register name. `efl` and `rflags` both map to the flags
    /// register. Returns `None` for unknown names.
    pub fn parse(name: &str) -> Option<Self> {
        match name {
            "rax" => Some(Self::Rax),
            "rbx" => Some(Self::Rbx),
            "rcx" => Some(Self::Rcx),
            "rdx" => Some(Self::Rdx),
            "rsi" => Some(Self::Rsi),
            "rdi" => Some(Self::Rdi),
            "rbp" => Some(Self::Rbp),
            "rsp" => Some(Self::Rsp),
            "r8" => Some(Self::R8),
            "r9" => Some(Self::R9),
            "r10" => Some(Self::R10),
            "r11" => Some(Self::R11),
            "r12" => Some(Self::R12),
            "r13" => Some(Self::R13),
            "r14" => Some(Self::R14),
            "r15" => Some(Self::R15),
            "rip" => Some(Self::Rip),
            "cs" => Some(Self::Cs),
            "ds" => Some(Self::Ds),
            "es" => Some(Self::Es),
            "fs" => Some(Self::Fs),
            "gs" => Some(Self::Gs),
            "ss" => Some(Self::Ss),
            "efl" | "rflags" => Some(Self::Efl),
            _ => None,
        }
    }
}

/// Runs `r` with a fully parsed target.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>,
    target: RTarget,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let registers = engine.vmi().registers();
    match target {
        RTarget::All => print_all(w, registers)?,
        RTarget::One(register) => writeln!(w, "{}", format_cell(registers, register))?,
    }
    Ok(())
}

/// Prints the compact WinDbg register dump: six rows of GP registers,
/// the mnemonic rflags line, and the segment-selector line.
fn print_all(w: &mut dyn Write, registers: &Registers) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let cell = |register| format_cell(registers, register);

    writeln!(
        w,
        "{} {} {}",
        cell(Register::Rax),
        cell(Register::Rbx),
        cell(Register::Rcx)
    )?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "{} {} {}",
        cell(Register::Rdx),
        cell(Register::Rsi),
        cell(Register::Rdi)
    )?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "{} {} {}",
        cell(Register::Rip),
        cell(Register::Rsp),
        cell(Register::Rbp)
    )?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "{} {} {}",
        cell(Register::R8),
        cell(Register::R9),
        cell(Register::R10)
    )?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "{} {} {}",
        cell(Register::R11),
        cell(Register::R12),
        cell(Register::R13)
    )?;
    writeln!(w, "{} {}", cell(Register::R14), cell(Register::R15))?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "iopl={}         {}",
        registers.rflags.io_privilege_level(),
        format_rflags_mnemonics(registers.rflags)
    )?;
    writeln!(
        w,
        "cs={:04x}  ss={:04x}  ds={:04x}  es={:04x}  fs={:04x}  gs={:04x}             efl={:08x}",
        registers.cs.selector.0,
        registers.ss.selector.0,
        registers.ds.selector.0,
        registers.es.selector.0,
        registers.fs.selector.0,
        registers.gs.selector.0,
        registers.rflags.0 as u32
    )?;

    Ok(())
}

/// Formats one `name=value` cell. Two-character GP names (`r8`, `r9`)
/// carry a leading space so that the three-column layout stays aligned.
fn format_cell(registers: &Registers, register: Register) -> String {
    match register {
        Register::Rax => format!("rax={:016x}", registers.rax),
        Register::Rbx => format!("rbx={:016x}", registers.rbx),
        Register::Rcx => format!("rcx={:016x}", registers.rcx),
        Register::Rdx => format!("rdx={:016x}", registers.rdx),
        Register::Rsi => format!("rsi={:016x}", registers.rsi),
        Register::Rdi => format!("rdi={:016x}", registers.rdi),
        Register::Rbp => format!("rbp={:016x}", registers.rbp),
        Register::Rsp => format!("rsp={:016x}", registers.rsp),
        Register::R8 => format!(" r8={:016x}", registers.r8),
        Register::R9 => format!(" r9={:016x}", registers.r9),
        Register::R10 => format!("r10={:016x}", registers.r10),
        Register::R11 => format!("r11={:016x}", registers.r11),
        Register::R12 => format!("r12={:016x}", registers.r12),
        Register::R13 => format!("r13={:016x}", registers.r13),
        Register::R14 => format!("r14={:016x}", registers.r14),
        Register::R15 => format!("r15={:016x}", registers.r15),
        Register::Rip => format!("rip={:016x}", registers.rip),
        Register::Cs => format!("cs={:04x}", registers.cs.selector.0),
        Register::Ds => format!("ds={:04x}", registers.ds.selector.0),
        Register::Es => format!("es={:04x}", registers.es.selector.0),
        Register::Fs => format!("fs={:04x}", registers.fs.selector.0),
        Register::Gs => format!("gs={:04x}", registers.gs.selector.0),
        Register::Ss => format!("ss={:04x}", registers.ss.selector.0),
        Register::Efl => format!("efl={:08x}", registers.rflags.0 as u32),
    }
}

/// Produces the WinDbg flags mnemonic string, e.g.
/// `nv up ei pl zr na pe nc` for all-cleared flags.
fn format_rflags_mnemonics(rflags: Rflags) -> String {
    let pairs: [(&str, &str, bool); 8] = [
        ("ov", "nv", rflags.overflow()),
        ("dn", "up", rflags.direction()),
        ("ei", "di", rflags.interrupt_enable()),
        ("ng", "pl", rflags.sign()),
        ("zr", "nz", rflags.zero()),
        ("ac", "na", rflags.auxiliary_carry()),
        ("pe", "po", rflags.parity()),
        ("cy", "nc", rflags.carry()),
    ];
    pairs
        .iter()
        .map(|&(set, clr, bit)| match bit {
            true => set,
            false => clr,
        })
        .collect::<Vec<_>>()
        .join(" ")
}

```

`src/cli/commands/thread.rs`:

```rs
//! `!thread` command handler.
//!
//! Mirrors WinDbg's `!thread [ThreadAddress [Flags]]`. Owns the shared
//! per-thread rendering that `!process` also uses.

use std::io::Write;

use vmi::{
    Va, VmiRead, VmiVa as _,
    arch::amd64::Amd64,
    os::{
        ProcessId, ThreadObject, VmiOsProcess as _, VmiOsThread as _,
        windows::{WindowsProcess, WindowsThread, WindowsThreadState},
    },
};

use super::{HelpEntry, k::KMode};
use crate::cli::{build_thread_context, engine::Engine, repl::ReplError};

/// Help text for `!thread`.
pub const HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[HelpEntry {
    syntax: "!thread  [Thread [Flags]]",
    summary: "Information about a thread or all threads.",
    extra: &["Thread: TID, ETHREAD addr, 0 (all), -1 (current)."],
}];

/// Target selector for `!thread`.
///
/// Mirrors `ProcessTarget`'s disambiguation so TIDs are usable even
/// though WinDbg accepts only an ETHREAD address.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum ThreadTarget {
    /// No `Thread` argument supplied.
    Default,

    /// Literal `-1`, the currently selected thread.
    Current,

    /// Literal `0`, every active thread in the system.
    All,

    /// Small hex value (<= `u32::MAX`), interpreted as a thread ID.
    Tid(u32),

    /// Hex value above `u32::MAX`, interpreted as an ETHREAD VA.
    Address(u64),
}

impl ThreadTarget {
    /// Returns WinDbg's documented default flag bitmask for `!thread`:
    /// `0x06` (WAIT_STATE | STACK), regardless of target.
    pub fn default_flags(&self) -> ThreadFlags {
        ThreadFlags::WAIT_STATE | ThreadFlags::STACK
    }
}

bitflags::bitflags! {
    /// WinDbg `!thread` flag bitmask. Bits align with `ProcessFlags`
    /// so `!process` can pass its flags through a masked conversion.
    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
    pub struct ThreadFlags: u64 {
        /// Thread wait states. No-op in the compact format since the
        /// state is always shown in the THREAD line.
        const WAIT_STATE     = 0x02;

        /// Stack trace. A no-op on its own. Combined with `WAIT_STATE`
        /// it triggers the stack walk.
        const STACK          = 0x04;

        /// Return address and stack pointer per frame, no arguments.
        const STACK_NOARGS   = 0x08;

        /// Switch the process context to the thread's owner before the
        /// stack walk.
        const SWITCH_CONTEXT = 0x10;
    }
}

/// Display options derived from the WinDbg flag bitmask.
struct Display {
    /// Show a stack trace under the thread.
    show_stacks: bool,

    /// Omit per-frame arguments from the stack trace.
    show_noargs: bool,

    /// Switch the process context for stack unwinding.
    switch_context: bool,
}

impl Display {
    /// Decodes the relevant bits out of the WinDbg flag bitmask.
    ///
    /// `WAIT_STATE | STACK` together request a stack. Either bit alone
    /// is a no-op.
    fn from_flags(flags: ThreadFlags) -> Self {
        let stack_bits = ThreadFlags::WAIT_STATE | ThreadFlags::STACK;
        Self {
            show_stacks: flags.contains(stack_bits),
            show_noargs: flags.contains(ThreadFlags::STACK_NOARGS),
            switch_context: flags.contains(ThreadFlags::SWITCH_CONTEXT),
        }
    }
}

/// Runs `!thread` with a fully parsed target.
pub fn run<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    target: ThreadTarget,
    flags: ThreadFlags,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    match target {
        ThreadTarget::Default | ThreadTarget::Current => {
            let thread = engine.current_thread();
            print_block(w, engine, thread, flags)?;
        }
        ThreadTarget::All => {
            print_all(w, engine, flags)?;
        }
        ThreadTarget::Tid(tid) => {
            let thread = find_by_tid(engine, tid)?;
            print_block(w, engine, thread, flags)?;
        }
        ThreadTarget::Address(va) => {
            print_block(w, engine, ThreadObject(Va(va)), flags)?;
        }
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Walks every active process, walks each process's thread list, and
/// prints every thread. Ctrl-C is checked between threads.
fn print_all<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    flags: ThreadFlags,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let mut thread_objects = Vec::new();
    for process in vmi.os().processes()? {
        let process = match process {
            Ok(process) => process,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read process while walking threads");
                continue;
            }
        };

        let threads = match process.threads() {
            Ok(threads) => threads,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread list");
                continue;
            }
        };

        for thread in threads {
            let thread = match thread {
                Ok(thread) => thread,
                Err(err) => {
                    tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread");
                    continue;
                }
            };
            match thread.object() {
                Ok(object) => thread_objects.push(object),
                Err(err) => tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread object"),
            }
        }
    }

    let show_stacks = Display::from_flags(flags).show_stacks;
    for thread_object in thread_objects {
        engine.check_interrupt()?;
        print_block(w, engine, thread_object, flags)?;
        if show_stacks {
            writeln!(w)?;
        }
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Looks up a thread by its TID by scanning every process's thread
/// list. Reads that fail for one thread do not abort the scan.
fn find_by_tid<Driver>(engine: &Engine<'_, Driver>, tid: u32) -> Result<ThreadObject, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    for process in vmi.os().processes()? {
        let process = match process {
            Ok(process) => process,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read process while searching by tid");
                continue;
            }
        };
        let threads = match process.threads() {
            Ok(threads) => threads,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread list while searching by tid");
                continue;
            }
        };
        for thread in threads {
            let thread = match thread {
                Ok(thread) => thread,
                Err(err) => {
                    tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread while searching by tid");
                    continue;
                }
            };
            match thread.id() {
                Ok(id) if id.0 == tid => return Ok(thread.object()?),
                Ok(_) => continue,
                Err(err) => {
                    tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read tid while searching by tid");
                    continue;
                }
            }
        }
    }
    Err(ReplError::ThreadNotFound(tid))
}

/// Prints one thread block, optionally followed by its stack trace.
pub fn print_block<Driver>(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    thread_object: ThreadObject,
    flags: ThreadFlags,
) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let display = Display::from_flags(flags);

    let vmi = engine.vmi();
    let thread = vmi.os().thread(thread_object)?;
    let owner_pid = match thread.process() {
        Ok(process) => process.id().ok(),
        Err(err) => {
            tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read owning process");
            None
        }
    };
    print_thread_line(w, &thread, owner_pid, display.show_stacks)?;

    if !display.show_stacks {
        return Ok(());
    }

    let target = match build_thread_context(&engine.vmi(), thread_object) {
        Ok(target) => target,
        Err(err) => {
            tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to build thread context");
            return Ok(());
        }
    };

    if display.switch_context {
        engine.switch_process(target.process_object)?;
    }

    let mode = match display.show_noargs {
        true => KMode::K,
        false => KMode::Kv,
    };
    super::k::run(w, engine, &target, mode, None, false)
}

/// Prints one thread row. `owner_pid` is the enclosing process's id.
/// When `show_details` is set the row is followed by the Owning/Attached/
/// Current block, matching WinDbg's layout for stack-bearing `!thread`.
fn print_thread_line(
    w: &mut dyn Write,
    thread: &impl VmiOsThreadExt,
    owner_pid: Option<ProcessId>,
    show_details: bool,
) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let owner = match owner_pid {
        Some(owner_pid) => format!("{owner_pid:x}"),
        None => "?".to_string(),
    };
    let thread_va = thread.object_va_display();
    let tid = thread.tid_display();
    let teb = thread.teb_display();
    let state = thread.state_display();

    writeln!(
        w,
        "THREAD {thread_va}  Cid {owner}.{tid}  Teb: {teb}  {state}"
    )?;

    if !show_details {
        return Ok(());
    }

    let owning = thread.owning_process_display();
    let current_sp = thread.current_sp_display();
    writeln!(w, "Owning Process   {owning}")?;
    if let Some(attached) = thread.attached_process_display() {
        writeln!(w, "Attached Process {attached}")?;
    }
    writeln!(w, "Current          {current_sp}")?;

    Ok(())
}

/// Maps `WindowsThreadState` to the WinDbg-style uppercase label.
fn format_state(state: WindowsThreadState) -> &'static str {
    match state {
        WindowsThreadState::Initialized => "INITIALIZED",
        WindowsThreadState::Ready => "READY",
        WindowsThreadState::Running => "RUNNING",
        WindowsThreadState::Standby => "STANDBY",
        WindowsThreadState::Terminated => "TERMINATED",
        WindowsThreadState::Waiting => "WAIT",
        WindowsThreadState::Transition => "TRANSITION",
        WindowsThreadState::DeferredReady => "DEFERRED_READY",
        WindowsThreadState::GateWaitObsolete => "GATEWAIT",
        WindowsThreadState::WaitingForProcessInSwap => "INSWAP",
        WindowsThreadState::Unknown(_) => "UNKNOWN",
    }
}

/// Formats `_KTHREAD.Alertable` the way WinDbg prints it.
fn format_alertable(alertable: bool) -> &'static str {
    match alertable {
        true => "Alertable",
        false => "Non-Alertable",
    }
}

/// Renders a `WindowsProcess` as `<eprocess>  Image: <name>`, the
/// compact form used for thread owner/attached labels.
fn format_process_short<Driver>(process: &WindowsProcess<'_, Driver>) -> String
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let addr = match process.object() {
        Ok(object) => format!("{object:x}"),
        Err(err) => {
            tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read process object");
            "?".to_string()
        }
    };
    let image = match process.name() {
        Ok(name) => name,
        Err(err) => {
            tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read image name");
            "?".to_string()
        }
    };
    format!("{addr}  Image: {image}")
}

/// Adapter trait over the VMI thread type. Each printable field is one
/// method returning a preformatted `String`. Reads that fail log at
/// debug and render as `?`. Reads that return `None` render as `-`.
trait VmiOsThreadExt {
    fn object_va_display(&self) -> String;
    fn tid_display(&self) -> String;
    fn teb_display(&self) -> String;
    fn state_display(&self) -> String;
    fn owning_process_display(&self) -> String;
    fn attached_process_display(&self) -> Option<String>;
    fn current_sp_display(&self) -> String;
}

impl<'a, Driver> VmiOsThreadExt for WindowsThread<'a, Driver>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    fn object_va_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.object() {
            Ok(object) => format!("{object:x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread object");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn tid_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.id() {
            Ok(tid) => format!("{tid:04x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read tid");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn teb_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.teb() {
            Ok(Some(teb)) => format!("{:016x}", teb.va()),
            Ok(None) => "-".to_string(),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read teb");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn state_display(&self) -> String {
        let state = match self.state() {
            Ok(state) => state,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread state");
                return "?".to_string();
            }
        };

        let label = format_state(state);
        if !matches!(state, WindowsThreadState::Waiting) {
            return label.to_string();
        }

        let reason = match self.wait_reason() {
            Ok(reason) => reason,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read wait reason");
                return label.to_string();
            }
        };

        let mut line = format!("{label}: ({reason:?})");
        match self.wait_mode() {
            Ok(mode) => line.push_str(&format!(" {mode:?}")),
            Err(err) => tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read wait mode"),
        }
        match self.alertable() {
            Ok(alertable) => line.push_str(&format!(" {}", format_alertable(alertable))),
            Err(err) => tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read alertable flag"),
        }
        line
    }

    fn owning_process_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.process() {
            Ok(process) => format_process_short(&process),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read owning process");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }

    fn attached_process_display(&self) -> Option<String> {
        match self.is_attached() {
            Ok(true) => match self.current_process() {
                Ok(process) => Some(format_process_short(&process)),
                Err(err) => {
                    tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read attached process");
                    Some("?".to_string())
                }
            },
            Ok(false) => None,
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read thread attach state");
                None
            }
        }
    }

    fn current_sp_display(&self) -> String {
        match self.kernel_stack() {
            Ok(sp) => format!("{sp:x}"),
            Err(err) => {
                tracing::debug!(%err, "failed to read kernel stack");
                "?".to_string()
            }
        }
    }
}
```

`src/cli/engine/mod.rs`:

```rs
//! Persistent debugger state: VMI session, ephemera lookups, current
//! process / thread / CPU, and the unwind targets for the REPL.

use std::sync::{
    Arc,
    atomic::{AtomicBool, Ordering},
};

use ephemera::{Ephemera, UnwindTarget};
use isr::{Profile, cache::IsrCache};
use vmi::{
    Architecture, VcpuId, VmiError, VmiRead, VmiSession, VmiState,
    arch::amd64::{Amd64, Cr3},
    driver::kdmp::Header64,
    os::{
        ProcessObject, ThreadObject, VmiOsProcess as _, VmiOsThread as _,
        windows::{ArchAdapter, WindowsOs, unwind::amd64::UnwindContextAmd64},
    },
};

use crate::cli::{build_cpu_context, find_crash_cpu, repl::ReplError};

/// Owns everything the REPL needs to run a command.
pub struct Engine<'a, Driver>
where
    Driver: VmiRead,
    Driver::Architecture: ArchAdapter<Driver>,
{
    /// The underlying VMI session.
    vmi: VmiSession<'a, WindowsOs<Driver>>,

    /// Register snapshot. `cr3` is rewritten by `switch_process`.
    registers: <Driver::Architecture as Architecture>::Registers,

    /// Kernel ISR profile.
    profile: Profile<'a>,

    /// Module, symbol, and process cache.
    ephemera: Ephemera<Driver>,

    /// Process whose CR3 is currently installed.
    current_process: ProcessObject,

    /// Currently selected thread.
    current_thread: ThreadObject,

    /// Currently selected processor. Drives the REPL prompt.
    current_cpu: VcpuId,

    /// Unwind target frozen at startup. Used by `!analyze`.
    crash_target: UnwindTarget,

    /// Dump header. Used by `!analyze`.
    header: Header64,

    /// Set by the Ctrl-C handler, cleared by the REPL between commands,
    /// polled by long-running commands via `check_interrupt`.
    interrupt: Arc<AtomicBool>,
}

impl<'a, Driver> Engine<'a, Driver>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
    Driver::Architecture: ArchAdapter<Driver>,
{
    /// Builds the engine and initialises state to the crash context.
    pub fn new(
        vmi: VmiState<'a, WindowsOs<Driver>>,
        isr: IsrCache,
        profile: Profile<'a>,
        header: Header64,
    ) -> Result<Self, VmiError> {
        let ephemera = Ephemera::new(vmi, isr)?;
        let crash_cpu = find_crash_cpu(&vmi)?;
        let crash_target = build_cpu_context(&vmi, crash_cpu)?;

        let mut engine = Self {
            vmi: *vmi.session(),
            registers: *vmi.registers(),
            profile,
            ephemera,
            current_process: ProcessObject::default(),
            current_thread: ThreadObject::default(),
            current_cpu: crash_cpu,
            crash_target: crash_target.clone(),
            header,
            interrupt: Arc::new(AtomicBool::new(false)),
        };

        engine.switch_process(crash_target.process_object)?;
        engine.switch_thread(crash_target.thread_object)?;
        engine.apply_unwind_context(&crash_target.context);

        Ok(engine)
    }

    /// Returns a VMI state view at the engine's current registers.
    pub fn vmi(&self) -> VmiState<'_, WindowsOs<Driver>> {
        self.vmi.with_registers(&self.registers)
    }

    /// Returns the module and symbol cache.
    pub fn ephemera(&self) -> &Ephemera<Driver> {
        &self.ephemera
    }

    /// Returns the kernel ISR profile.
    pub fn profile(&self) -> &Profile<'a> {
        &self.profile
    }

    /// Returns the currently selected process.
    pub fn current_process(&self) -> ProcessObject {
        self.current_process
    }

    /// Returns the currently selected thread.
    pub fn current_thread(&self) -> ThreadObject {
        self.current_thread
    }

    /// Returns the currently selected processor.
    pub fn current_cpu(&self) -> VcpuId {
        self.current_cpu
    }

    /// Synthesizes an unwind target from the current process, thread,
    /// and register snapshot. Reflects the most recent `.thread` or `~N`.
    pub fn current_target(&self) -> UnwindTarget {
        UnwindTarget {
            process_object: self.current_process,
            thread_object: self.current_thread,
            context: UnwindContextAmd64::from(&self.registers),
        }
    }

    /// Returns the crash unwind target frozen at startup.
    pub fn crash_target(&self) -> &UnwindTarget {
        &self.crash_target
    }

    /// Returns the dump header.
    pub fn header(&self) -> &Header64 {
        &self.header
    }

    /// Returns a clone of the interrupt flag for the Ctrl-C handler.
    pub fn interrupt_flag(&self) -> Arc<AtomicBool> {
        Arc::clone(&self.interrupt)
    }

    /// Clears the interrupt flag.
    pub fn clear_interrupt(&self) {
        self.interrupt.store(false, Ordering::SeqCst);
    }

    /// Returns `Err(ReplError::Interrupted)` if a Ctrl-C arrived since
    /// the last `clear_interrupt`.
    pub fn check_interrupt(&self) -> Result<(), ReplError> {
        match self.interrupt.load(Ordering::SeqCst) {
            true => Err(ReplError::Interrupted),
            false => Ok(()),
        }
    }

    /// Sets the current process context by rewriting CR3 to the
    /// process's translation root.
    pub fn switch_process(&mut self, process: ProcessObject) -> Result<(), VmiError> {
        let process = self.vmi().os().process(process)?;
        let translation_root = process.translation_root()?;

        self.current_process = process.object()?;
        self.registers.cr3 = Cr3(translation_root.0);

        Ok(())
    }

    /// Sets the current thread context.
    pub fn switch_thread(&mut self, thread: ThreadObject) -> Result<(), VmiError> {
        let thread = self.vmi().os().thread(thread)?;

        self.current_thread = thread.object()?;

        Ok(())
    }

    /// Switches to the given processor and applies its saved register
    /// state.
    pub fn switch_cpu(&mut self, cpu: VcpuId) -> Result<(), VmiError> {
        let target = build_cpu_context(&self.vmi(), cpu)?;

        self.switch_process(target.process_object)?;
        self.switch_thread(target.thread_object)?;
        self.apply_unwind_context(&target.context);
        self.current_cpu = cpu;

        Ok(())
    }

    /// Writes an unwind context into the register snapshot. Touches
    /// only the fields the unwinder cares about - RIP, RSP, RBP, and
    /// the AMD64 callee-saved registers. Other fields keep their
    /// existing values.
    pub fn apply_unwind_context(&mut self, context: &UnwindContextAmd64) {
        self.registers.rip = context.rip;
        self.registers.rsp = context.rsp;
        self.registers.rbp = context.rbp;
        self.registers.rbx = context.rbx;
        self.registers.rsi = context.rsi;
        self.registers.rdi = context.rdi;
        self.registers.r12 = context.r12;
        self.registers.r13 = context.r13;
        self.registers.r14 = context.r14;
        self.registers.r15 = context.r15;
    }
}
```

`src/cli/format.rs`:

```rs
//! WinDbg-compatible output formatting.
//!
//! Provides functions to format addresses and symbols in the style
//! used by WinDbg, including the backtick address format and the
//! `module!function+0xNN` notation.

use std::borrow::Cow;

use ephemera::ResolvedSymbol;
use msvc_demangler::DemangleFlags;
use vmi::Va;

/// Formats a virtual address in WinDbg backtick style.
///
/// Example: `fffff801`6ec2ac46`
pub struct FormatVa(pub Va);

impl std::fmt::Display for FormatVa {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter) -> std::fmt::Result {
        let raw = self.0.0;
        //if raw == 0 {
        //    return write!(f, "0");
        //}
        let high = (raw >> 32) as u32;
        let low = raw as u32;
        write!(f, "{high:08x}`{low:08x}")
    }
}

/// Returns the WinDbg-style display name for a module.
///
/// Kernel executables are shown as "nt"; other modules have their
/// file extension stripped.
pub struct FormatModuleName<'a>(pub &'a str);

impl std::fmt::Display for FormatModuleName<'_> {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter) -> std::fmt::Result {
        if self.0.eq_ignore_ascii_case("ntoskrnl.exe")
            || self.0.eq_ignore_ascii_case("ntkrnlmp.exe")
        {
            return write!(f, "nt");
        }

        // Strip the file extension.
        match self.0.rfind('.') {
            Some(pos) => write!(f, "{}", &self.0[..pos]),
            None => write!(f, "{}", self.0),
        }
    }
}

/// Formats a resolved symbol in WinDbg notation.
///
/// Returns `module!function+0xNN` when a function name is known,
/// or `module+0xNN` as a fallback.
pub struct FormatSymbol<'a>(pub &'a ResolvedSymbol);

impl std::fmt::Display for FormatSymbol<'_> {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter) -> std::fmt::Result {
        let module_name = &self.0.module_name;
        let function_name = &self.0.function_name;
        let offset = self.0.offset;

        if module_name.is_empty() && function_name.is_empty() {
            write!(f, "0x{}", FormatVa(Va(offset)))?;
            return Ok(());
        }

        write!(f, "{}", FormatModuleName(module_name))?;

        if !function_name.is_empty() {
            let flags = DemangleFlags::COMPLETE
                | DemangleFlags::SPACE_AFTER_COMMA
                | DemangleFlags::HUG_TYPE
                | DemangleFlags::NO_MS_KEYWORDS
                | DemangleFlags::NO_CLASS_TYPE
                | DemangleFlags::NO_FUNCTION_RETURNS
                | DemangleFlags::NAME_ONLY;

            let symbol = msvc_demangler::demangle(function_name, flags)
                .map(Cow::Owned)
                .unwrap_or_else(|_| Cow::Borrowed(function_name));

            write!(f, "!{symbol}")?;
        }

        if offset != 0 {
            write!(f, "+0x{offset:x}")?;
        }

        Ok(())
    }
}
```
