`src/cli/mod.rs`:

```rs
//! Top-level CLI.

mod bugcheck;
mod commands;
mod engine;
mod format;
mod output;
mod repl;

use std::{path::PathBuf, sync::Mutex};

use anyhow::{Context as _, Result};
use clap::Parser;
use ephemera::UnwindTarget;
use indicatif::{ProgressBar, ProgressStyle};
use isr::{cache::IsrCache, download::ProgressEvent};
use vmi::{
    VcpuId, VmiCore, VmiError, VmiRead, VmiSession, VmiState, VmiVa as _,
    arch::amd64::Amd64,
    driver::kdmp::VmiKdmpDriver,
    os::{
        ThreadObject, VmiOsProcess as _, VmiOsThread as _,
        windows::{
            WindowsContext as _, WindowsOs, WindowsOsExt as _, WindowsThread, WindowsThreadState,
            unwind::amd64::UnwindContextAmd64,
        },
    },
};
use zerocopy::{FromBytes, IntoBytes};

use crate::cli::{engine::Engine, repl::DispatchOutcome};

/// Ephemera. Windows crash dump analysis tool.
#[derive(Parser)]
#[command(name = "ephemera")]
struct Cli {
    /// Path to the crash dump file.
    dump: PathBuf,

    /// ISR cache directory.
    #[arg(long, default_value = "cache")]
    cache: PathBuf,

    /// Only use already-cached artifacts. Never reach out to the network.
    #[arg(long)]
    offline: bool,

    /// Run a one-shot command and stay in the REPL afterward.
    #[arg(short = 'i', long)]
    interactive: bool,

    /// Command to run. Anything after `--` on the command line.
    #[arg(last = true)]
    command: Vec<String>,
}

/// Runs the CLI.
pub fn run() -> Result<()> {
    tracing_subscriber::fmt()
        .with_env_filter(tracing_subscriber::EnvFilter::from_default_env())
        .with_ansi(false)
        .init();

    let cli = Cli::parse();

    let driver = VmiKdmpDriver::<Amd64>::new(&cli.dump)?;
    let core = VmiCore::new(driver)?;
    let registers = core.registers(VcpuId(0))?;

    let kernel_info = WindowsOs::find_kernel(&core, &registers)?
        .context("kernel information not found in dump")?;
    tracing::info!(?kernel_info, "kernel information");

    let isr = IsrCache::new(&cli.cache)?
        .with_offline(cli.offline)
        .with_progress(progress_reporter());
    let entry = isr.entry_from_codeview(kernel_info.codeview)?;
    let profile = unsafe { entry.profile_unchecked()? };
    let os =
        WindowsOs::<VmiKdmpDriver<Amd64>>::with_kernel_base(&profile, kernel_info.base_address)?;
    let session = VmiSession::new(&core, &os);
    let state = session.with_registers(&registers);

    let header = core.driver().header();
    let mut engine = Engine::new(state, isr, profile, header)?;

    let one_shot = cli.command.join(" ");
    let has_one_shot = !one_shot.trim().is_empty();

    if has_one_shot {
        match repl::run_line(&mut engine, &one_shot) {
            Ok(DispatchOutcome::Exit) => return Ok(()),
            Ok(DispatchOutcome::Continue) => {}
            Err(err) => {
                eprintln!("error: {err}");
                if !cli.interactive {
                    std::process::exit(1);
                }
            }
        }
    }

    if cli.interactive || !has_one_shot {
        repl::run(&mut engine)?;
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Builds a progress-reporting closure for the ISR cache.
fn progress_reporter() -> impl Fn(ProgressEvent) + Send + Sync + 'static {
    let bar = Mutex::<Option<ProgressBar>>::new(None);
    move |event| {
        let mut guard = bar.lock().unwrap();
        match event {
            ProgressEvent::DownloadStarted { url, total_bytes } => {
                let name = url
                    .path_segments()
                    .and_then(|mut segs| segs.next_back())
                    .unwrap_or(url.as_str());
                *guard = Some(progress_bar(total_bytes, format!("downloading {name}")));
            }
            ProgressEvent::ExtractStarted { path, total_bytes } => {
                let name = path
                    .file_name()
                    .map(|name| name.to_string_lossy())
                    .unwrap_or("file".into());
                *guard = Some(progress_bar(total_bytes, format!("extracting {name}")));
            }
            ProgressEvent::DownloadProgress { bytes, .. }
            | ProgressEvent::ExtractProgress { bytes, .. } => {
                if let Some(bar) = guard.as_ref() {
                    bar.set_position(bytes);
                }
            }
            ProgressEvent::DownloadComplete { .. } | ProgressEvent::ExtractComplete { .. } => {
                if let Some(bar) = guard.take() {
                    bar.finish_and_clear();
                }
            }
        }
    }
}

/// Creates an indicatif progress bar.
fn progress_bar(total_bytes: Option<u64>, message: String) -> ProgressBar {
    let bar = match total_bytes {
        Some(total) => {
            let bar = ProgressBar::new(total);
            bar.set_style(
                ProgressStyle::with_template(
                    "{msg} [{bar:40.cyan/blue}] {bytes}/{total_bytes} ({eta})",
                )
                .unwrap()
                .progress_chars("=> "),
            );
            bar
        }
        None => {
            let bar = ProgressBar::new_spinner();
            bar.set_style(ProgressStyle::with_template("{spinner} {msg} {bytes}").unwrap());
            bar
        }
    };
    bar.set_message(message);
    bar
}

/// AMD64 KSWITCH_FRAME (Windows 10/11).
#[allow(missing_docs, non_camel_case_types, non_snake_case)]
#[repr(C)]
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, FromBytes, IntoBytes)]
struct KSWITCH_FRAME_AMD64 {
    P1Home: u64,
    P2Home: u64,
    P3Home: u64,
    P4Home: u64,
    P5Home: u64,
    ApcBypass: u8,
    Fill1: [u8; 7],
    Rbp: u64,
    Return: u64,
}

/// Builds an unwind context for a thread, sourcing registers from the
/// CPU it runs on when it is RUNNING and from its saved KSWITCH_FRAME
/// otherwise. Mirrors WinDbg's `TargetInfo::GetContextFromThreadStack`.
pub fn build_thread_context<Driver>(
    vmi: &VmiState<WindowsOs<Driver>>,
    thread: ThreadObject,
) -> Result<UnwindTarget, VmiError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let thread = vmi.os().thread(thread)?;
    let process = thread.process()?;

    let thread_object = thread.object()?;
    let process_object = process.object()?;

    let context = match thread.state()? {
        WindowsThreadState::Running => running_thread_context(vmi, &thread)?,
        _ => parked_thread_context(vmi, &thread)?,
    };

    Ok(UnwindTarget {
        process_object,
        thread_object,
        context,
    })
}

/// Builds a running thread's unwind context from its current CPU's
/// saved `_KPRCB.Context`. `_KTHREAD.NextProcessor` identifies the CPU,
/// matching the field WinDbg's `!thread` prints as "RUNNING on processor N".
fn running_thread_context<Driver>(
    vmi: &VmiState<WindowsOs<Driver>>,
    thread: &WindowsThread<Driver>,
) -> Result<UnwindContextAmd64, VmiError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let cpu = thread.next_processor()?;
    let kprcb = vmi.os().kprcb(cpu)?;
    let context = kprcb.processor_context()?;

    Ok(UnwindContextAmd64 {
        rip: context.rip(),
        rsp: context.rsp(),
        rbp: context.rbp(),
        rbx: context.rbx(),
        rsi: context.rsi(),
        rdi: context.rdi(),
        r12: context.r12().unwrap_or(0),
        r13: context.r13().unwrap_or(0),
        r14: context.r14().unwrap_or(0),
        r15: context.r15().unwrap_or(0),
    })
}

/// Builds a non-running thread's unwind context from the `KSWITCH_FRAME`
/// the scheduler pushed at `_KTHREAD.KernelStack` during the last context
/// switch.
fn parked_thread_context<Driver>(
    vmi: &VmiState<WindowsOs<Driver>>,
    thread: &WindowsThread<Driver>,
) -> Result<UnwindContextAmd64, VmiError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let kernel_stack = thread.kernel_stack()?;
    let switch_frame = match vmi.read_struct::<KSWITCH_FRAME_AMD64>(kernel_stack) {
        Ok(switch_frame) => switch_frame,
        Err(err) => {
            tracing::error!(%err, "kernel stack not resident");
            return Err(err);
        }
    };

    Ok(UnwindContextAmd64 {
        rip: switch_frame.Return,
        rsp: kernel_stack.0 + size_of::<KSWITCH_FRAME_AMD64>() as u64,
        rbp: switch_frame.Rbp,
        rbx: 0,
        rsi: 0,
        rdi: 0,
        r12: 0,
        r13: 0,
        r14: 0,
        r15: 0,
    })
}

/// Locates the processor whose saved RSP matches the dump's crash RSP.
pub fn find_crash_cpu<Driver>(vmi: &VmiState<WindowsOs<Driver>>) -> Result<VcpuId, VmiError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let crash_rsp = vmi.registers().rsp;
    let num_cpus = vmi.os().number_of_processors()?;

    for cpu in 0..num_cpus {
        let kprcb = vmi.os().kprcb(VcpuId(cpu))?;
        if let Ok(ctx) = kprcb.processor_context()
            && ctx.rsp() == crash_rsp
        {
            tracing::info!(cpu, "found crash CPU");
            return Ok(VcpuId(cpu));
        }
    }

    tracing::debug!("no CPU matched crash RSP, falling back to CPU 0");
    Ok(VcpuId(0))
}

/// Builds an unwind context from a specific CPU's saved processor state.
pub fn build_cpu_context<Driver>(
    vmi: &VmiState<WindowsOs<Driver>>,
    cpu: VcpuId,
) -> Result<UnwindTarget, VmiError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let kprcb = vmi.os().kprcb(cpu)?;
    tracing::info!(%cpu, kprcb = %kprcb.va(), "found KPRCB");

    let thread = kprcb.current_thread()?;
    let process = thread.process()?;
    let context = kprcb.processor_context()?;

    let thread_object = thread.object()?;
    let process_object = process.object()?;

    Ok(UnwindTarget {
        process_object,
        thread_object,
        context: UnwindContextAmd64 {
            rip: context.rip(),
            rsp: context.rsp(),
            rbp: context.rbp(),
            rbx: context.rbx(),
            rsi: context.rsi(),
            rdi: context.rdi(),
            r12: context.r12().unwrap_or(0),
            r13: context.r13().unwrap_or(0),
            r14: context.r14().unwrap_or(0),
            r15: context.r15().unwrap_or(0),
        },
    })
}

```

`src/cli/output.rs`:

```rs
//! Line-prefixing writer used to indent nested command output.
//!
//! Every command's `run` takes `w: &mut dyn Write` as its first argument
//! and emits through `writeln!(w, ...)`. Callers nest by wrapping the
//! writer in an [`IndentWriter`] before passing it down, or pass the
//! writer unchanged to keep the current depth.

use std::io::{self, Write};

/// Writer that prepends `prefix` at the start of every line it emits.
///
/// The invariant it relies on is that every `\n` means end-of-line. As
/// long as callers only emit whole lines (i.e. `writeln!`), wrapping is
/// always well-defined. Doing partial-line `write!` calls and then
/// nesting another `IndentWriter` around the same sink would inject the
/// nested prefix mid-line.
pub struct IndentWriter<'w> {
    inner: &'w mut dyn Write,
    prefix: Vec<u8>,
    at_line_start: bool,
}

impl<'w> IndentWriter<'w> {
    /// Wraps `inner` so that every line written through it is prefixed
    /// with `width` spaces.
    pub fn new(inner: &'w mut dyn Write, width: usize) -> Self {
        Self {
            inner,
            prefix: vec![b' '; width],
            at_line_start: true,
        }
    }
}

impl Write for IndentWriter<'_> {
    fn write(&mut self, buf: &[u8]) -> io::Result<usize> {
        let mut written = 0;
        for chunk in buf.split_inclusive(|&b| b == b'\n') {
            if self.at_line_start && chunk != b"\n" && !chunk.is_empty() {
                self.inner.write_all(&self.prefix)?;
            }
            self.inner.write_all(chunk)?;
            self.at_line_start = chunk.ends_with(b"\n");
            written += chunk.len();
        }
        Ok(written)
    }

    fn flush(&mut self) -> io::Result<()> {
        self.inner.flush()
    }
}

```

`src/cli/repl/command.rs`:

```rs
//! The parsed command type that sits between the pure parser and the
//! impure dispatcher.

use vmi::{Va, VcpuId};

use crate::cli::commands::{
    d::{DFormat, Range},
    k::KMode,
    process::{ProcessFlags, ProcessTarget},
    r::RTarget,
    thread::{ThreadFlags, ThreadTarget},
};

/// One REPL command.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum Command {
    /// `!analyze`.
    BangAnalyze,

    /// `!process [Process [Flags [ImageName]]]`.
    BangProcess {
        /// Which process or set of processes to print.
        target: ProcessTarget,

        /// WinDbg-style bitmask. The parser substitutes the documented
        /// per-target default when the user omits the argument.
        flags: ProcessFlags,

        /// Image-name filter. Only meaningful when `target` is
        /// [`ProcessTarget::All`].
        image: Option<String>,
    },

    /// `!thread [Thread [Flags]]`.
    BangThread {
        /// Which thread or set of threads to print.
        target: ThreadTarget,

        /// WinDbg-style bitmask. The parser substitutes `0x06`
        /// (WAIT_STATE | STACK) when the user omits the argument.
        flags: ThreadFlags,
    },

    /// `d{b|d|q|p|ps} [Address [L<Count> | Address2]]`.
    D {
        /// Selected sub-command plus any per-variant flags.
        format: DFormat,

        /// Parsed address range.
        range: Range,
    },

    /// `dt <type> [address]`.
    Dt {
        /// Symbol name, unvalidated.
        type_name: String,

        /// Optional memory address to read.
        address: Option<Va>,
    },

    /// `k`, `kb`, `kc`, `kv`, each with an optional frame count.
    K {
        /// Column layout selected by the command suffix.
        mode: KMode,

        /// Cap on the number of frames printed.
        frame_count: Option<u32>,
    },

    /// `r [Reg]` and the `r<Reg>` no-space form.
    R {
        /// Full dump or a single register.
        target: RTarget,
    },

    /// `.process [/r] [/p] <address>`. Switches are parsed and ignored.
    DotProcess { address: Va },

    /// `.thread [/r] [/p] <address>`. Switches are parsed and ignored.
    DotThread { address: Va },

    /// `~<n>`. Changes the current processor.
    Tilde { cpu: VcpuId },

    /// `.help`, `help`, or `?`.
    Help,

    /// `q`, `quit`, or `.quit`.
    Quit,
}

```

`src/cli/repl/completer.rs`:

```rs
//! rustyline helper: command-name and `dt` type-name completion, no
//! hinting, no highlight.

use isr::Profile;
use rustyline::{
    Context, Helper, Result,
    completion::{Completer, Pair},
    highlight::Highlighter,
    hint::Hinter,
    validate::Validator,
};

/// Static list of completable command names.
#[rustfmt::skip]
const COMMANDS: &[&str] = &[
    "!analyze",
    "!process",
    "!thread",
    "?",
    ".help",
    ".process",
    ".quit",
    ".thread",
    "db",
    "dd",
    "dp",
    "dps",
    "dq",
    "dt",
    "help",
    "k",
    "kb",
    "kc",
    "kv",
    "q",
    "quit",
    "r",
];

/// Completer for the REPL. Completes the first token of a segment
/// against the command list, and the second token of a `dt` segment
/// against the profile's struct names.
pub struct ReplHelper {
    /// Snapshot of struct names from the kernel profile, sorted.
    types: Vec<String>,
}

impl ReplHelper {
    /// Builds a helper with a type-name snapshot taken from `profile`.
    pub fn new(profile: &Profile<'_>) -> Self {
        let mut types = profile
            .structs()
            .map(|s| s.name().to_string())
            .collect::<Vec<_>>();
        types.sort_unstable();
        Self { types }
    }
}

/// Returns true if `s` starts with `prefix`, treating ASCII letters
/// case-insensitively. Non-ASCII bytes compare exactly.
fn starts_with_ignore_ascii_case(s: &str, prefix: &str) -> bool {
    let s = s.as_bytes();
    let prefix = prefix.as_bytes();
    s.len() >= prefix.len() && s[..prefix.len()].eq_ignore_ascii_case(prefix)
}

impl Completer for ReplHelper {
    type Candidate = Pair;

    fn complete(&self, line: &str, pos: usize, _ctx: &Context<'_>) -> Result<(usize, Vec<Pair>)> {
        let head = &line[..pos];

        // Start of the token being typed.
        let token_start = head
            .rfind(|head: char| head.is_whitespace() || head == ';')
            .map(|token_start| token_start + 1)
            .unwrap_or(0);
        let prefix = &head[token_start..];

        // Start of the current `;`-terminated segment.
        let segment_start = head
            .rfind(';')
            .map(|segment_start| segment_start + 1)
            .unwrap_or(0);
        let segment_head = head[segment_start..token_start].trim();

        let candidates = if segment_head.is_empty() {
            COMMANDS
                .iter()
                .copied()
                .filter(|candidate| candidate.starts_with(prefix))
                .map(str::to_string)
                .collect::<Vec<_>>()
        }
        else if segment_head == "dt" {
            self.types
                .iter()
                .filter(|candidate| starts_with_ignore_ascii_case(candidate, prefix))
                .cloned()
                .collect::<Vec<_>>()
        }
        else {
            return Ok((pos, Vec::new()));
        };

        let pairs = candidates
            .into_iter()
            .map(|candidate| Pair {
                display: candidate.clone(),
                replacement: candidate,
            })
            .collect();

        Ok((token_start, pairs))
    }
}

impl Hinter for ReplHelper {
    type Hint = String;
}

impl Highlighter for ReplHelper {}
impl Validator for ReplHelper {}
impl Helper for ReplHelper {}

```

`src/cli/repl/dispatch.rs`:

```rs
//! Command dispatch. The only place that mutates the engine.

use std::io::Write;

use vmi::{
    VmiRead,
    arch::amd64::Amd64,
    os::{ProcessObject, ThreadObject},
};

use crate::cli::{
    build_thread_context, commands,
    commands::HelpEntry,
    engine::Engine,
    repl::{Command, ReplError},
};

/// Help text for the REPL built-ins that have no dedicated command module.
const BUILTIN_HELP: &[HelpEntry] = &[
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: ".process [/r] [/p] <address>",
        summary: "Set the process context.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: ".thread  [/r] [/p] <address>",
        summary: "Set the register context to a thread.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "~<n>",
        summary: "Change the current processor.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: ".help, help, ?",
        summary: "Show this list.",
        extra: &[],
    },
    HelpEntry {
        syntax: "q, quit, .quit",
        summary: "Exit the REPL.",
        extra: &[],
    },
];

/// Outcome of dispatching one command.
pub enum DispatchOutcome {
    /// Continue the REPL loop.
    Continue,

    /// Exit the REPL loop.
    Exit,
}

/// Runs a single parsed command, applying side effects to `engine`.
pub fn dispatch<Driver>(
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    command: Command,
) -> Result<DispatchOutcome, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let stdout = std::io::stdout();
    let mut w = stdout.lock();

    match command {
        Command::BangAnalyze => {
            let target = engine.crash_target().clone();
            let header = *engine.header();
            commands::analyze::run(&mut w, engine, &target, &header)?;
        }
        Command::BangProcess {
            target,
            flags,
            image,
        } => {
            commands::process::run(&mut w, engine, target, flags, image.as_deref())?;
        }
        Command::BangThread { target, flags } => {
            commands::thread::run(&mut w, engine, target, flags)?;
        }
        Command::D { format, range } => {
            commands::d::run(&mut w, engine, format, range)?;
        }
        Command::Dt { type_name, address } => {
            commands::dt::run(&mut w, engine, engine.profile(), &type_name, address)?;
        }
        Command::K { mode, frame_count } => {
            let target = engine.current_target();
            commands::k::run(&mut w, engine, &target, mode, frame_count, true)?;
        }
        Command::R { target } => {
            commands::r::run(&mut w, engine, target)?;
        }
        Command::DotProcess { address } => {
            engine.switch_process(ProcessObject(address))?;
        }
        Command::DotThread { address } => {
            let target = build_thread_context(&engine.vmi(), ThreadObject(address))?;
            engine.switch_process(target.process_object)?;
            engine.switch_thread(target.thread_object)?;
            engine.apply_unwind_context(&target.context);
        }
        Command::Tilde { cpu } => {
            engine.switch_cpu(cpu)?;
        }
        Command::Help => print_help(&mut w)?,
        Command::Quit => return Ok(DispatchOutcome::Exit),
    }

    Ok(DispatchOutcome::Continue)
}

/// Prints the command list, pulling each row from its owning module.
fn print_help(w: &mut dyn Write) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    let groups: &[&[HelpEntry]] = &[
        commands::analyze::HELP,
        commands::process::HELP,
        commands::thread::HELP,
        commands::dt::HELP,
        commands::d::HELP,
        commands::k::HELP,
        commands::r::HELP,
        BUILTIN_HELP,
    ];

    let width = groups
        .iter()
        .flat_map(|group| group.iter())
        .map(|entry| entry.syntax.len())
        .max()
        .unwrap_or(0);

    writeln!(w, "Commands:")?;
    for entry in groups.iter().flat_map(|group| group.iter()) {
        writeln!(w, "  {:<width$}  {}", entry.syntax, entry.summary)?;
        for line in entry.extra {
            writeln!(w, "  {:<width$}  {}", "", line)?;
        }
    }

    Ok(())
}

```

`src/cli/repl/error.rs`:

```rs
//! Error type shared by the REPL loop, parser, dispatch, and commands.

use vmi::VmiError;

use crate::cli::repl::parser::ParseError;

/// Errors surfaced at or below the REPL boundary.
#[derive(thiserror::Error, Debug)]
pub enum ReplError {
    /// Parser rejected the input line.
    #[error(transparent)]
    Parse(#[from] ParseError),

    /// VMI read or lookup failed.
    #[error(transparent)]
    Vmi(#[from] VmiError),

    /// No process with the given PID was found in the active process list.
    #[error("process not found: pid {0}")]
    ProcessNotFound(u32),

    /// No thread with the given TID was found in the active process list.
    #[error("thread not found: tid {0:x}")]
    ThreadNotFound(u32),

    /// Address expression referenced a register that is not an address
    /// (segment selector, `efl`) or otherwise cannot be resolved.
    #[error("bad address: {0}")]
    BadAddress(String),

    /// `module!name` did not resolve to a known kernel symbol.
    #[error("symbol not found: {0}")]
    SymbolNotFound(String),

    /// User requested cancellation via Ctrl-C during a running command.
    #[error("interrupted")]
    Interrupted,

    /// History file I/O or other OS error.
    #[error(transparent)]
    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),

    /// Readline error that is not `Eof` or `Interrupted` special-cased above.
    #[error(transparent)]
    Readline(#[from] rustyline::error::ReadlineError),

    /// `ctrlc` crate failed to install its signal handler.
    #[error(transparent)]
    CtrlC(#[from] ctrlc::Error),
}

```

`src/cli/repl/mod.rs`:

```rs
//! Interactive WinDbg-style REPL.

pub mod command;
pub mod completer;
pub mod dispatch;
pub mod error;
pub mod parser;

use std::{path::PathBuf, sync::atomic::Ordering};

pub use command::Command;
pub use dispatch::{DispatchOutcome, dispatch};
pub use error::ReplError;
use rustyline::{Editor, error::ReadlineError};
use vmi::{VmiRead, arch::amd64::Amd64};

use crate::cli::{engine::Engine, repl::completer::ReplHelper};

/// Enters the interactive loop. Returns when the user quits or EOF fires.
pub fn run<Driver>(engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>) -> Result<(), ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    let history = history_path();
    if let Some(parent) = history.parent() {
        std::fs::create_dir_all(parent)?;
    }

    let flag = engine.interrupt_flag();
    let ctrlc_flag = flag.clone();
    ctrlc::set_handler(move || ctrlc_flag.store(true, Ordering::SeqCst))?;

    let mut editor = Editor::<ReplHelper, _>::new()?;
    editor.set_helper(Some(ReplHelper::new(engine.profile())));
    let _ = editor.load_history(&history);

    loop {
        engine.clear_interrupt();
        let prompt = format!("{}: kd> ", engine.current_cpu());

        match editor.readline(&prompt) {
            Ok(line) => {
                let trimmed = line.trim();
                if trimmed.is_empty() {
                    continue;
                }
                let _ = editor.add_history_entry(trimmed);
                match run_line(engine, trimmed) {
                    Ok(DispatchOutcome::Exit) => break,
                    Ok(DispatchOutcome::Continue) => {}
                    Err(err) => eprintln!("error: {err}"),
                }
            }
            Err(ReadlineError::Interrupted) => continue,
            Err(ReadlineError::Eof) => break,
            Err(err) => return Err(err.into()),
        }
    }

    let _ = editor.save_history(&history);
    Ok(())
}

/// Parses a line and runs every resulting command. Stops on the first
/// error or on `DispatchOutcome::Exit`.
pub fn run_line<Driver>(
    engine: &mut Engine<'_, Driver>,
    line: &str,
) -> Result<DispatchOutcome, ReplError>
where
    Driver: VmiRead<Architecture = Amd64>,
{
    for command in parser::parse_line(line)? {
        match dispatch(engine, command)? {
            DispatchOutcome::Exit => return Ok(DispatchOutcome::Exit),
            DispatchOutcome::Continue => {}
        }
    }
    Ok(DispatchOutcome::Continue)
}

/// Returns the REPL history file path. Falls back to a relative path
/// when `HOME` is unset.
fn history_path() -> PathBuf {
    match std::env::var_os("HOME") {
        Some(home) => PathBuf::from(home).join(".ephemera").join("history"),
        None => PathBuf::from(".ephemera_history"),
    }
}

```

`src/cli/repl/parser.rs`:

```rs
//! Pure parser turning REPL input lines into commands.
//!
//! Parsing is independent of the engine and of any dump state. The
//! full grammar fits in this file.

use vmi::{Va, VcpuId};

use crate::cli::{
    commands::{
        d::{AddrExpr, DFormat, Range},
        k::KMode,
        process::{ProcessFlags, ProcessTarget},
        r::{RTarget, Register},
        thread::{ThreadFlags, ThreadTarget},
    },
    repl::command::Command,
};

/// Errors produced by [`parse_line`].
#[derive(thiserror::Error, Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
pub enum ParseError {
    /// Input ended inside a quoted string.
    #[error("unterminated quote")]
    UnterminatedQuote,

    /// First token did not match any known command.
    #[error("unknown command: {0}")]
    UnknownCommand(String),

    /// Token expected to be a number could not be parsed under any of the
    /// accepted prefixes (`0n` decimal, `0x` hex, bare hex).
    #[error("invalid number: {0}")]
    BadNumber(String),

    /// Required positional argument was not provided.
    #[error("{0}: missing argument")]
    MissingArg(&'static str),

    /// More positional arguments were provided than the command accepts.
    #[error("{0}: too many arguments")]
    TooManyArgs(&'static str),

    /// A flag that is not recognised by the command.
    #[error("unknown flag: {0}")]
    BadFlag(String),

    /// Command-specific semantic error. `command` is the head token,
    /// `detail` is a short static description of what was wrong.
    #[error("{command}: {detail}")]
    Command {
        command: &'static str,
        detail: &'static str,
    },
}

/// Parses a whole input line into a list of commands.
///
/// Splits on `;` outside quotes before tokenizing. An empty line
/// yields an empty vector. Any parse error aborts the whole line.
pub fn parse_line(line: &str) -> Result<Vec<Command>, ParseError> {
    let mut commands = Vec::new();
    for segment in split_on_semicolon(line) {
        let trimmed = segment.trim();
        if trimmed.is_empty() {
            continue;
        }
        let tokens = match shlex::split(trimmed) {
            Some(tokens) => tokens,
            None => return Err(ParseError::UnterminatedQuote),
        };
        if tokens.is_empty() {
            continue;
        }
        commands.push(parse_one(&tokens)?);
    }
    Ok(commands)
}

/// Splits `line` on `;` characters that are not inside single or
/// double quotes.
fn split_on_semicolon(line: &str) -> Vec<&str> {
    let mut segments = Vec::new();
    let mut in_single = false;
    let mut in_double = false;
    let mut start = 0;

    for (i, ch) in line.char_indices() {
        match ch {
            '\'' if !in_double => in_single = !in_single,
            '"' if !in_single => in_double = !in_double,
            ';' if !in_single && !in_double => {
                segments.push(&line[start..i]);
                start = i + 1;
            }
            _ => {}
        }
    }
    segments.push(&line[start..]);
    segments
}

/// Dispatches one segment to its per-command parser.
fn parse_one(tokens: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    // parse_line never produces empty segments.
    let head = tokens[0].as_str();
    let rest = &tokens[1..];

    match head {
        "!analyze" => parse_bang_analyze(rest),
        "!process" => parse_bang_process(rest),
        "!thread" => parse_bang_thread(rest),
        "db" => parse_d(DFormat::Db, rest),
        "dd" => parse_d(
            DFormat::Dd {
                show_symbols: false,
            },
            rest,
        ),
        "dq" => parse_d(
            DFormat::Dq {
                show_symbols: false,
            },
            rest,
        ),

        // dp / dps are aliases for dq / dqs on 64-bit Amd64. A future
        // 32-bit backend will remap these to DFormat::Dd.
        "dp" => parse_d(
            DFormat::Dq {
                show_symbols: false,
            },
            rest,
        ),
        "dps" => parse_d(DFormat::Dq { show_symbols: true }, rest),
        "dt" => parse_dt(rest),
        "k" => parse_k(rest),
        "r" => parse_r(rest),
        ".process" => parse_dot_process(rest),
        ".thread" => parse_dot_thread(rest),
        ".help" | "help" | "?" => parse_zero_arg(rest, Command::Help, "help"),
        "q" | "quit" | ".quit" => parse_zero_arg(rest, Command::Quit, "quit"),
        other if other.starts_with('~') => parse_tilde(other),
        other if other.starts_with('k') => parse_k_prefixed(other, rest),
        other if other.starts_with('r') => parse_r_prefixed(other, rest),
        other => Err(ParseError::UnknownCommand(other.to_string())),
    }
}

fn parse_bang_analyze(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    parse_zero_arg(rest, Command::BangAnalyze, "!analyze")
}

fn parse_bang_process(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    if rest.len() > 3 {
        return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("!process"));
    }
    let target = match rest.first() {
        Some(arg) if arg == "-1" => ProcessTarget::Current,
        Some(arg) => {
            let value = parse_number(arg)?;
            if value == 0 {
                ProcessTarget::All
            }
            else if value <= u64::from(u32::MAX) {
                ProcessTarget::Pid(value as u32)
            }
            else {
                ProcessTarget::Address(value)
            }
        }
        None => ProcessTarget::Default,
    };
    let flags = match rest.get(1) {
        Some(flags) => ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(parse_number(flags)?),
        None => target.default_flags(),
    };
    let image = match rest.get(2) {
        Some(image) => {
            if !matches!(target, ProcessTarget::All) {
                return Err(ParseError::Command {
                    command: "!process",
                    detail: "image name requires process 0",
                });
            }
            Some(image.clone())
        }
        None => None,
    };
    Ok(Command::BangProcess {
        target,
        flags,
        image,
    })
}

fn parse_bang_thread(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    if rest.len() > 2 {
        return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("!thread"));
    }
    let target = match rest.first() {
        Some(arg) if arg == "-1" => ThreadTarget::Current,
        Some(arg) => {
            let value = parse_number(arg)?;
            if value == 0 {
                ThreadTarget::All
            }
            else if value <= u64::from(u32::MAX) {
                ThreadTarget::Tid(value as u32)
            }
            else {
                ThreadTarget::Address(value)
            }
        }
        None => ThreadTarget::Default,
    };
    let flags = match rest.get(1) {
        Some(flags) => ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(parse_number(flags)?),
        None => target.default_flags(),
    };
    Ok(Command::BangThread { target, flags })
}

fn parse_dt(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    let type_name = match rest.first() {
        Some(type_name) => type_name.clone(),
        None => return Err(ParseError::MissingArg("dt")),
    };
    let address = match rest.get(1) {
        Some(address) => Some(parse_number_va(address)?),
        None => None,
    };
    if rest.len() > 2 {
        return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("dt"));
    }
    Ok(Command::Dt { type_name, address })
}

/// Parses the spaced `k [Mode] [FrameCount]` form. The first rest arg
/// is treated as a mode letter when it matches `b`, `c`, or `v`, and as
/// the frame count otherwise.
fn parse_k(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    let (mode, tail) = match rest.first() {
        Some(arg) => match KMode::parse(arg) {
            Some(mode) => (mode, &rest[1..]),
            None => (KMode::K, rest),
        },
        None => (KMode::K, rest),
    };
    parse_k_tail(mode, tail)
}

/// Parses the no-space `k<Mode>` form. `head` has already been verified
/// to start with `k`. Falls back to an `UnknownCommand` error when the
/// suffix is not a mode letter.
fn parse_k_prefixed(head: &str, rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    let mode = match KMode::parse(&head[1..]) {
        Some(mode) => mode,
        None => return Err(ParseError::UnknownCommand(head.to_string())),
    };
    parse_k_tail(mode, rest)
}

/// Reads the optional frame count that follows the `k` mode selection.
fn parse_k_tail(mode: KMode, rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    if rest.len() > 1 {
        return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("k"));
    }
    let frame_count = match rest.first() {
        Some(arg) => {
            let value = parse_number(arg)?;
            if value > u64::from(u32::MAX) {
                return Err(ParseError::Command {
                    command: "k",
                    detail: "frame count out of range",
                });
            }
            Some(value as u32)
        }
        None => None,
    };
    Ok(Command::K { mode, frame_count })
}
fn parse_dot_process(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    Ok(Command::DotProcess {
        address: parse_dot_switches(rest, ".process")?,
    })
}

fn parse_dot_thread(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    Ok(Command::DotThread {
        address: parse_dot_switches(rest, ".thread")?,
    })
}

/// Consumes `/r` and `/p` flags in any order, then expects a single
/// hex address. Flags are accepted and ignored.
fn parse_dot_switches(rest: &[String], name: &'static str) -> Result<Va, ParseError> {
    let mut address: Option<Va> = None;

    for token in rest {
        match token.as_str() {
            "/r" | "/p" => {}
            flag if flag.starts_with('/') => {
                return Err(ParseError::BadFlag(flag.to_string()));
            }
            value => match address {
                None => address = Some(parse_number_va(value)?),
                Some(_) => return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs(name)),
            },
        }
    }

    match address {
        Some(address) => Ok(address),
        None => Err(ParseError::MissingArg(name)),
    }
}
/// Parses the spaced `r [Reg]` form.
fn parse_r(rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    if rest.len() > 1 {
        return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("r"));
    }
    let target = match rest.first() {
        Some(name) => match Register::parse(name) {
            Some(register) => RTarget::One(register),
            None => {
                return Err(ParseError::Command {
                    command: "r",
                    detail: "unknown register",
                });
            }
        },
        None => RTarget::All,
    };
    Ok(Command::R { target })
}

/// Parses the no-space `r<Reg>` form. `head` has already been verified
/// to start with `r`. Falls back to an `UnknownCommand` error when the
/// suffix is not a register name.
fn parse_r_prefixed(head: &str, rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    let register = match Register::parse(&head[1..]) {
        Some(register) => register,
        None => return Err(ParseError::UnknownCommand(head.to_string())),
    };
    if !rest.is_empty() {
        return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("r"));
    }
    Ok(Command::R {
        target: RTarget::One(register),
    })
}

/// Parses the body of a `d*` command after the format has been
/// selected by the dispatch table.
fn parse_d(format: DFormat, rest: &[String]) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    let range = match rest.len() {
        0 => return Err(ParseError::MissingArg("d")),
        1 => Range::Single(parse_addr_expr(&rest[0])?),
        2 => {
            let second = &rest[1];
            match second
                .strip_prefix('L')
                .or_else(|| second.strip_prefix('l'))
            {
                Some(count) => {
                    if count.is_empty() {
                        return Err(ParseError::Command {
                            command: "d",
                            detail: "empty count after L",
                        });
                    }
                    let value = parse_number(count)?;
                    if value > u64::from(u32::MAX) {
                        return Err(ParseError::Command {
                            command: "d",
                            detail: "count out of range",
                        });
                    }
                    Range::Count(parse_addr_expr(&rest[0])?, value as u32)
                }
                None => Range::End(parse_addr_expr(&rest[0])?, parse_addr_expr(second)?),
            }
        }
        _ => return Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs("d")),
    };

    Ok(Command::D { format, range })
}

fn parse_tilde(head: &str) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    let digits = &head[1..];
    if digits.is_empty() || !digits.chars().all(|digits| digits.is_ascii_digit()) {
        return Err(ParseError::UnknownCommand(head.to_string()));
    }
    let cpu = match digits.parse::<u16>() {
        Ok(cpu) => cpu,
        Err(_) => return Err(ParseError::UnknownCommand(head.to_string())),
    };
    Ok(Command::Tilde { cpu: VcpuId(cpu) })
}

/// Parses a zero-argument command, returning `TooManyArgs` if any
/// tokens remain.
fn parse_zero_arg(
    rest: &[String],
    command: Command,
    name: &'static str,
) -> Result<Command, ParseError> {
    match rest.is_empty() {
        true => Ok(command),
        false => Err(ParseError::TooManyArgs(name)),
    }
}

/// Parses a number under WinDbg's prefix conventions.
///
/// `0n<digits>` is decimal. `0x<hex>` / `0X<hex>` is hex. A bare digit
/// run is hex (WinDbg default). Backticks inside the digit run are
/// stripped before conversion.
fn parse_number(raw: &str) -> Result<u64, ParseError> {
    let bad = || ParseError::BadNumber(raw.to_string());

    let (digits, radix) = match raw.strip_prefix("0n").or_else(|| raw.strip_prefix("0N")) {
        Some(rest) => (rest, 10),
        None => {
            let hex = raw
                .strip_prefix("0x")
                .or_else(|| raw.strip_prefix("0X"))
                .unwrap_or(raw);
            (hex, 16)
        }
    };

    if digits.is_empty() {
        return Err(bad());
    }

    let cleaned = match radix {
        16 => digits.replace('`', ""),
        _ => digits.to_string(),
    };

    match u64::from_str_radix(&cleaned, radix) {
        Ok(cleaned) => Ok(cleaned),
        Err(_) => Err(bad()),
    }
}

/// Parses a number into a `Va`.
fn parse_number_va(raw: &str) -> Result<Va, ParseError> {
    Ok(Va(parse_number(raw)?))
}

/// Parses a single-token address expression into [`AddrExpr`].
///
/// Grammar: atom (`+` | `-` atom)*, left-associative. Atoms are
/// classified as register, number, or symbol.
fn parse_addr_expr(s: &str) -> Result<AddrExpr, ParseError> {
    if s.is_empty() {
        return Err(bad_addr());
    }

    let tokens = lex_addr(s)?;
    let mut iter = tokens.into_iter();

    let first = match iter.next() {
        Some(AddrToken::Atom(atom)) => classify_atom(&atom)?,
        Some(AddrToken::Op(_)) => return Err(bad_addr()),
        None => return Err(bad_addr()),
    };

    let mut expr = first;
    loop {
        let op = match iter.next() {
            Some(AddrToken::Op(op)) => op,
            Some(AddrToken::Atom(_)) => return Err(bad_addr()),
            None => break,
        };
        let rhs_atom = match iter.next() {
            Some(AddrToken::Atom(atom)) => atom,
            Some(AddrToken::Op(_)) => return Err(bad_addr()),
            None => return Err(bad_addr()),
        };
        let rhs = classify_atom(&rhs_atom)?;
        expr = match op {
            '+' => AddrExpr::Add(Box::new(expr), Box::new(rhs)),
            '-' => AddrExpr::Sub(Box::new(expr), Box::new(rhs)),
            _ => return Err(bad_addr()),
        };
    }

    Ok(expr)
}

/// Output of `lex_addr`. Atom strings are handed to `classify_atom`
/// for register / number / symbol tagging.
enum AddrToken {
    Atom(String),
    Op(char),
}

/// Splits the expression string into alternating atom / operator
/// tokens. `+` and `-` are the only operators. Backticks inside an
/// atom are preserved for the number parser to strip.
fn lex_addr(s: &str) -> Result<Vec<AddrToken>, ParseError> {
    let mut out = Vec::new();
    let mut current = String::new();
    for ch in s.chars() {
        match ch {
            '+' | '-' => {
                if current.is_empty() {
                    return Err(bad_addr());
                }
                out.push(AddrToken::Atom(std::mem::take(&mut current)));
                out.push(AddrToken::Op(ch));
            }
            _ => current.push(ch),
        }
    }
    if !current.is_empty() {
        out.push(AddrToken::Atom(current));
    }
    Ok(out)
}

/// Classifies one atom string as register, number, or symbol per the
/// rules in the design spec.
fn classify_atom(atom: &str) -> Result<AddrExpr, ParseError> {
    // Leading '@' forces register.
    if let Some(name) = atom.strip_prefix('@') {
        return match Register::parse(name) {
            Some(register) => Ok(AddrExpr::Register(register)),
            None => Err(ParseError::Command {
                command: "d",
                detail: "unknown register",
            }),
        };
    }

    // Contains '!': always a symbol. Empty module means nt.
    if let Some(bang) = atom.find('!') {
        let module = &atom[..bang];
        let name = &atom[bang + 1..];
        if name.is_empty() {
            return Err(bad_addr());
        }
        let qualified = match module.is_empty() {
            true => format!("nt!{name}"),
            false => atom.to_string(),
        };
        return Ok(AddrExpr::Symbol(qualified));
    }

    // Bare register name.
    if let Some(register) = Register::parse(atom) {
        return Ok(AddrExpr::Register(register));
    }

    // Otherwise try number, fall through to implied-kernel symbol.
    match parse_number(atom) {
        Ok(value) => Ok(AddrExpr::Number(value)),
        Err(_) => Ok(AddrExpr::Symbol(format!("nt!{atom}"))),
    }
}

fn bad_addr() -> ParseError {
    ParseError::Command {
        command: "d",
        detail: "bad address expression",
    }
}

#[cfg(test)]
mod tests {
    use super::*;

    #[test]
    fn empty_line_yields_no_commands() {
        assert_eq!(parse_line("").unwrap(), Vec::<Command>::new());
        assert_eq!(parse_line("   ").unwrap(), Vec::<Command>::new());
        assert_eq!(parse_line(";;;").unwrap(), Vec::<Command>::new());
    }

    #[test]
    fn unknown_command_is_rejected() {
        let err = parse_line("nope").unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::UnknownCommand(ref token) if token == "nope"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn unterminated_quote_is_rejected() {
        let err = parse_line("dt \"open").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::UnterminatedQuote);
    }

    #[test]
    fn help_variants_parse() {
        for input in ["help", ".help", "?"] {
            assert_eq!(parse_line(input).unwrap(), vec![Command::Help]);
        }
    }

    #[test]
    fn quit_variants_parse() {
        for input in ["q", "quit", ".quit"] {
            assert_eq!(parse_line(input).unwrap(), vec![Command::Quit]);
        }
    }

    #[test]
    fn help_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line("help me").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs("help"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_analyze_parses() {
        assert_eq!(parse_line("!analyze").unwrap(), vec![Command::BangAnalyze]);
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_analyze_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line("!analyze foo").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs("!analyze"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dt_parses_type_only() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("dt _EPROCESS").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::Dt {
                type_name: "_EPROCESS".to_string(),
                address: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dt_parses_type_and_address() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("dt _EPROCESS 0xffff8001").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::Dt {
                type_name: "_EPROCESS".to_string(),
                address: Some(Va(0xffff8001)),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dt_requires_type() {
        let err = parse_line("dt").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::MissingArg("dt"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dt_rejects_bad_address() {
        let err = parse_line("dt _EPROCESS zzz").unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::BadNumber(ref raw) if raw == "zzz"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dt_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line("dt _EPROCESS 0xff 0xee").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs("dt"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn k_parses() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("k").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::K {
                mode: KMode::K,
                frame_count: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn kb_parses() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("kb").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::K {
                mode: KMode::Kb,
                frame_count: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn kc_parses() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("kc").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::K {
                mode: KMode::Kc,
                frame_count: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn kv_parses() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("kv").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::K {
                mode: KMode::Kv,
                frame_count: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn k_parses_frame_count() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("k 10").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::K {
                mode: KMode::K,
                frame_count: Some(0x10),
            }],
        );
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("kv 0x20").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::K {
                mode: KMode::Kv,
                frame_count: Some(0x20),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn k_rejects_bad_frame_count() {
        let err = parse_line("k zzz").unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::BadNumber(ref raw) if raw == "zzz"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn k_rejects_out_of_range_frame_count() {
        let err = parse_line("k 100000000").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(
            err,
            ParseError::Command {
                command: "k",
                detail: "frame count out of range",
            },
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn k_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line("k 10 20").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs("k"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_no_args() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::Default,
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x03),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_zero_is_all() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process 0").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::All,
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x03),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_minus_one_is_current() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process -1").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::Current,
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x03),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_small_hex_is_pid() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process 4").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::Pid(4),
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x0f),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process ffffffff").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::Pid(0xffff_ffff),
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x0f),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_large_hex_is_address() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process ffff800100000000").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::Address(0xffff_8001_0000_0000),
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x0f),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_with_flags() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process 0 7").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::All,
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x07),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_explicit_zero_flags_clears_default() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process 0 0").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::All,
                flags: ProcessFlags::empty(),
                image: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_with_image_filter() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!process 0 7 lsass.exe").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangProcess {
                target: ProcessTarget::All,
                flags: ProcessFlags::from_bits_retain(0x07),
                image: Some("lsass.exe".to_string()),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_image_requires_all() {
        let err = parse_line("!process 4 7 lsass.exe").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(
            err,
            ParseError::Command {
                command: "!process",
                detail: "image name requires process 0",
            },
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_process_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line("!process 0 7 foo bar").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs("!process"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dot_process_plain() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line(".process ffff8001").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::DotProcess {
                address: Va(0xffff8001)
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dot_process_with_switches() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line(".process /r /p ffff8001").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::DotProcess {
                address: Va(0xffff8001)
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dot_process_rejects_bad_flag() {
        let err = parse_line(".process /x ffff8001").unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::BadFlag(ref flag) if flag == "/x"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dot_process_requires_address() {
        let err = parse_line(".process").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::MissingArg(".process"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dot_process_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line(".process ffff8001 deadbeef").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs(".process"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn dot_thread_with_switches() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line(".thread /r /p ffff8001").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::DotThread {
                address: Va(0xffff8001)
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn tilde_parses_cpu_zero() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("~0").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::Tilde { cpu: VcpuId(0) }]
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn tilde_parses_multi_digit() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("~15").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::Tilde { cpu: VcpuId(15) }]
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn tilde_without_digits_is_unknown() {
        let err = parse_line("~").unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::UnknownCommand(ref token) if token == "~"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn tilde_with_non_digit_is_unknown() {
        let err = parse_line("~0s").unwrap_err();
        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::UnknownCommand(ref token) if token == "~0s"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn semicolon_chains_commands() {
        let parsed = parse_line("dt _EPROCESS 0xff ; k ; ~2").unwrap();
        assert_eq!(
            parsed,
            vec![
                Command::Dt {
                    type_name: "_EPROCESS".to_string(),
                    address: Some(Va(0xff)),
                },
                Command::K {
                    mode: KMode::K,
                    frame_count: None,
                },
                Command::Tilde { cpu: VcpuId(2) },
            ],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn semicolon_inside_quotes_is_preserved() {
        // `dt "a;b"` has one argument with a literal semicolon.
        let parsed = parse_line("dt \"a;b\"").unwrap();
        assert_eq!(
            parsed,
            vec![Command::Dt {
                type_name: "a;b".to_string(),
                address: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn quoted_type_name_is_accepted() {
        let parsed = parse_line("dt \"my type\"").unwrap();
        assert_eq!(
            parsed,
            vec![Command::Dt {
                type_name: "my type".to_string(),
                address: None,
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_no_args() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Default,
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x06),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_minus_one_is_current() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread -1").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Current,
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x06),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_zero_is_all() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread 0").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::All,
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x06),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_small_hex_is_tid() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread 3e0").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Tid(0x3e0),
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x06),
            }],
        );
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread ffffffff").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Tid(0xffff_ffff),
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x06),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_large_hex_is_address() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread ffffd486be575080").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Address(0xffff_d486_be57_5080),
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x06),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_with_flags() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread -1 2").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Current,
                flags: ThreadFlags::from_bits_retain(0x02),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_explicit_zero_flags_clears_default() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("!thread -1 0").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::BangThread {
                target: ThreadTarget::Current,
                flags: ThreadFlags::empty(),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn bang_thread_rejects_extra_args() {
        let err = parse_line("!thread -1 0 foo").unwrap_err();
        assert_eq!(err, ParseError::TooManyArgs("!thread"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_hex_bare() {
        assert_eq!(parse_number("2a").unwrap(), 0x2a);
        assert_eq!(parse_number("FFFF").unwrap(), 0xffff);
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_hex_0x_prefix() {
        assert_eq!(parse_number("0x2a").unwrap(), 0x2a);
        assert_eq!(parse_number("0X2A").unwrap(), 0x2a);
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_decimal_0n_prefix() {
        assert_eq!(parse_number("0n42").unwrap(), 42);
        assert_eq!(parse_number("0n0").unwrap(), 0);
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_backticks_stripped() {
        assert_eq!(parse_number("ffff`aaaa").unwrap(), 0xffff_aaaa);
        assert_eq!(parse_number("0xffff`aaaa").unwrap(), 0xffff_aaaa);
        assert_eq!(
            parse_number("fffffb88`b60c3038").unwrap(),
            0xffff_fb88_b60c_3038,
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_rejects_empty_prefix() {
        assert!(matches!(parse_number("0x"), Err(ParseError::BadNumber(_))));
        assert!(matches!(parse_number("0n"), Err(ParseError::BadNumber(_))));
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_rejects_mixed_prefix() {
        assert!(matches!(
            parse_number("0n0xff"),
            Err(ParseError::BadNumber(_)),
        ));
    }

    #[test]
    fn number_rejects_non_decimal_after_0n() {
        assert!(matches!(
            parse_number("0nabc"),
            Err(ParseError::BadNumber(_))
        ));
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_bare_register() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("rsp").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp),
        );
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("rip").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rip),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_at_register() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("@rsp").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_number() {
        assert_eq!(parse_addr_expr("0xff").unwrap(), AddrExpr::Number(0xff),);
        assert_eq!(parse_addr_expr("ff").unwrap(), AddrExpr::Number(0xff),);
        assert_eq!(parse_addr_expr("0n42").unwrap(), AddrExpr::Number(42),);
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("ffff`aaaa").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Number(0xffff_aaaa),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_symbol_qualified() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("nt!KiDispatchException").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Symbol("nt!KiDispatchException".to_string()),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_symbol_empty_module_means_nt() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("!KiDispatchException").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Symbol("nt!KiDispatchException".to_string()),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_symbol_bare_implies_nt() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("KiDispatchException").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Symbol("nt!KiDispatchException".to_string()),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_add() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("rsp+80").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Add(
                Box::new(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp)),
                Box::new(AddrExpr::Number(0x80)),
            ),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_sub() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("rsp-20").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Sub(
                Box::new(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp)),
                Box::new(AddrExpr::Number(0x20)),
            ),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_left_associative() {
        // (rsp + 10) - 4
        assert_eq!(
            parse_addr_expr("rsp+10-4").unwrap(),
            AddrExpr::Sub(
                Box::new(AddrExpr::Add(
                    Box::new(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp)),
                    Box::new(AddrExpr::Number(0x10)),
                )),
                Box::new(AddrExpr::Number(4)),
            ),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_rejects_trailing_op() {
        assert!(parse_addr_expr("rsp+").is_err());
        assert!(parse_addr_expr("rsp-").is_err());
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_rejects_leading_op() {
        assert!(parse_addr_expr("+rsp").is_err());
    }

    #[test]
    fn addr_expr_rejects_empty() {
        assert!(parse_addr_expr("").is_err());
    }

    #[test]
    fn db_parses_single_address() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("db ffff").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Db,
                range: Range::Single(AddrExpr::Number(0xffff)),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn db_parses_with_count() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("db ffff L5").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Db,
                range: Range::Count(AddrExpr::Number(0xffff), 5),
            }],
        );
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("db ffff l0n16").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Db,
                range: Range::Count(AddrExpr::Number(0xffff), 16),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn db_parses_end_address_range() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("db ffff ffff+10").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Db,
                range: Range::End(
                    AddrExpr::Number(0xffff),
                    AddrExpr::Add(
                        Box::new(AddrExpr::Number(0xffff)),
                        Box::new(AddrExpr::Number(0x10)),
                    ),
                ),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn db_rejects_missing_address() {
        assert_eq!(parse_line("db").unwrap_err(), ParseError::MissingArg("d"));
    }

    #[test]
    fn db_rejects_too_many_args() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("db a b c").unwrap_err(),
            ParseError::TooManyArgs("d"),
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn db_rejects_empty_count() {
        assert!(parse_line("db ffff L").is_err());
    }

    #[test]
    fn dd_maps_to_dd_format() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("dd @rsp").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Dd {
                    show_symbols: false
                },
                range: Range::Single(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp)),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dq_maps_to_dq_format() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("dq @rsp").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Dq {
                    show_symbols: false
                },
                range: Range::Single(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp)),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dp_is_alias_for_dq_on_amd64() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("dp @rsp").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Dq {
                    show_symbols: false
                },
                range: Range::Single(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp)),
            }],
        );
    }

    #[test]
    fn dps_is_alias_for_dq_with_symbols() {
        assert_eq!(
            parse_line("dps @rsp L5").unwrap(),
            vec![Command::D {
                format: DFormat::Dq { show_symbols: true },
                range: Range::Count(AddrExpr::Register(Register::Rsp), 5),
            }],
        );
    }
}

```

`src/lib.rs`:

```rs
mod module;
mod process;
mod resolver;
mod walkstack;

use std::cell::RefCell;

use isr::cache::IsrCache;
use vmi::{
    Va, VmiError, VmiRead, VmiState,
    os::{
        ProcessObject,
        windows::{ArchAdapter, WindowsOs},
    },
};

pub use self::{
    module::ModuleEntry,
    process::{ProcessEntry, ProcessManager, ProcessPreloadFlags},
    resolver::{ImageEntry, ResolvedSymbol, Resolver, ResolverError},
    walkstack::{UnwindTarget, WalkFrame, walk_stack},
};

/// Analysis session holding VMI state, ISR cache, kernel modules, and
/// per-process state.
pub struct Ephemera<Driver>
where
    Driver: VmiRead,
    Driver::Architecture: ArchAdapter<Driver>,
{
    processes: ProcessManager,
    resolver: RefCell<Resolver<Driver>>,
}

impl<Driver> Ephemera<Driver>
where
    Driver: VmiRead,
    Driver::Architecture: ArchAdapter<Driver>,
{
    /// Creates a new session by enumerating kernel modules and processes.
    pub fn new(vmi: VmiState<'_, WindowsOs<Driver>>, isr: IsrCache) -> Result<Self, VmiError> {
        let processes = ProcessManager::new(vmi, ProcessPreloadFlags::empty())?;

        Ok(Self {
            processes,
            resolver: RefCell::new(Resolver::new(isr)),
        })
    }

    pub fn get_process(&self, process_object: ProcessObject) -> Option<ProcessEntry> {
        self.processes.get(process_object)
    }

    pub fn lookup_module(
        &self,
        vmi: VmiState<'_, WindowsOs<Driver>>,
        process_object: ProcessObject,
        va: Va,
    ) -> Result<Option<ModuleEntry>, VmiError> {
        self.processes.lookup_module(vmi, process_object, va)
    }

    /// Returns the cached PE binary for the given module, downloading
    /// it from the symbol server if needed.
    pub fn resolve_image(&self, module: &ModuleEntry) -> Option<ImageEntry> {
        let mut resolver = self.resolver.borrow_mut();
        resolver.resolve_image(module)
    }

    /// Resolves a virtual address to a symbol within the given module.
    ///
    /// Lazily loads PDB symbols for the module on first access.
    /// Falls back to module+offset if the PDB cannot be loaded.
    pub fn resolve_symbol(
        &self,
        vmi: VmiState<'_, WindowsOs<Driver>>,
        module: &ModuleEntry,
        va: Va,
    ) -> ResolvedSymbol {
        let mut resolver = self.resolver.borrow_mut();
        resolver.resolve_symbol(vmi, module, va)
    }
}

```

`src/main.rs`:

```rs
//! Ephemera - a crash dump analysis tool.
//!
//! Reads a Windows crash dump and produces WinDbg-compatible output
//! such as stack backtraces (kb).

mod cli;

fn main() -> Result<(), anyhow::Error> {
    cli::run()
}
```
